The Statement 'Like a Free Person' and Emancipation
Statement of ruling with explanation of non-emancipatory nature

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the phrase 'You are like a free person' when said to a slave and explain why it does not effect emancipation.

Core Idea
Calling a slave 'like a free person' honors his status but does not set him free.

This lesson examines a specific statement of comparison ('You are like a free person') and its legal effect in Hanafi fiqh. The ruling is that such a statement does not constitute emancipation, even if it conveys honor. Understanding this distinction is important because Hanafi law requires explicit or clearly indicative words for a valid declaration of freedom.

Guided Path
1
Identify the statement and its context
The statement is 'You are like a free person' said by a master to his slave. Recognize that it is a comparison, not a direct declaration.
Focus on the wording: 'mithl al-hurr' means 'like a free person'.
2
Determine the apparent meaning
The text explains that the meaning is about honor, respect, and greatness, not legal status. Identify that the speaker intends praise.
The phrase is a compliment, not a legal act.
3
Connect to the legal ruling
The Hanafi ruling is that the slave is not freed. The statement does not effect emancipation because it lacks the necessary explicitness.
Emancipation requires sarih (explicit) words like 'you are free' or clear kinayah.
4
Analyze the rationale
The rationale is that the words do not indicate a transfer of legal status. They are merely a comparison in attributes. The intention of the speaker is not to free.
Even if the master intended emancipation, the phrase is insufficient per Hanafi rules.
5
Note cross-madhhab implications
Some other schools might consider the master's intention and interpret the phrase as emancipation, but Hanafis require clear wording to protect the slave's status from casual statements.
This ikhtilaf is mentioned in the source's mukhtalaf_fih note.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۱۹۹] (۱۰) اگر اپنے غلام سے کہا تم آزاد کی طرح ہو تو آزاد نہیں ہوگا۔
تم آزاد کی طرح ہو کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ تم آزاد کی طرح ہو شرافت تعظیم اور بزرگی میں۔ اس لئے اس جملے سے آزاد کرنا مقصود نہیں ہے اس
لئے آزاد نہیں ہوگا۔
[2199] (10) If he says to his slave 'You are like a free person', he is not freed. The meaning of 'You are like a free person' is that you are like a free person in honor, respect, and greatness. Therefore, emancipation is not intended by this sentence, so he is not freed.
Source pages p. 244

Commentary
This is a straightforward ruling statement. The author clarifies that saying a slave is 'like a free person' is understood as a compliment regarding dignity or character, not as an actual statement of emancipation. Since the words do not directly or indirectly indicate freeing, no legal effect occurs. This follows the general Hanafi principle that emancipation is a serious legal consequence requiring explicit or clearly indicative words.

Key Terms
مثل الحر (mithl al-hurr): Like a free person; used as a comparison in honor or status.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the phrase 'You are like a free person' mean according to the text?
A) The slave is actually free
B) The slave is compared to a free person in honor and respect, not in legal status
C) The master intends to free the slave
D) The slave is a mahram

Key Takeaway
The phrase 'You are like a free person' is a compliment, not a legal emancipation, and does not free the slave in Hanafi fiqh.

How Exclusive Language Emancipates: The Ruling on 'You Are Nothing But Free'
Statement of ruling with explanation of explicit emancipation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the phrase 'ma anta illa hurr' and explain why exclusive wording (hasr) makes emancipation explicit.

Core Idea
Exclusive wording using 'illa' makes emancipation unmistakably clear, freeing the slave immediately.

In Hanafi fiqh, the words used to free a slave must clearly express the master's intent. This lesson examines a particularly strong formulation: 'You are nothing but free' (ma anta illa hurr). The inclusive exclusivity created by 'illa' leaves no room for doubt, and the ruling is that the slave is freed as an obvious consequence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the phrase and its structure
The phrase 'ma anta illa hurr' combines negation (ma), subject (anta), exceptive particle (illa), and predicate (hurr). The combination creates hasr (exclusivity).
Recognize that 'illa' is the key element.
2
Understand the legal effect of hasr
In Hanafi usul, hasr makes the meaning exclusive and binding. Here it asserts that the slave is nothing other than free.
Hasr removes any ambiguity.
3
Apply the ruling
Because the intent to free is clear, the slave becomes free immediately upon utterance.
No further conditions are needed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۲۲۰۰] (۱۱) اور اگر کہا نہیں ہو تم مگر آزاد تو آزاد ہو جائے گا۔
اگر کہا کہ نہیں ہو تم مگر آزاد تو اس جملے سے غلام آزاد ہو جائے گا۔ اس جملے میں حصر کے ساتھ آزاد کرنا ہی مقصود ہے اس لئے بدرجہ اولی آزاد ہوگا۔
[2200] (11) And if he says 'You are nothing but free', he will be freed. If he says 'You are nothing but free', then by this sentence the slave will be freed. In this sentence, with exclusivity ('illa'), emancipation is clearly intended, so he will be freed as an obvious result.
Source pages p. 244

Commentary
This is a simple ruling statement. The author explains that when the master uses an exclusionary phrase 'You are nothing but free' (ma anta illa hurr), the word 'illa' (except/nothing but) creates a strong assertion of freedom. This is considered a clear and explicit declaration of emancipation, and thus the slave becomes free. The phrase 'bil-darajat al-ula' (as a first-degree/obvious result) indicates that such wording is even more forceful than ordinary statements of freeing.

Key Terms
حصر (hasr): Exclusivity or restriction achieved by the word 'illa' (except/nothing but), emphasizing that the slave is only free and nothing else.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does saying 'You are nothing but free' free the slave?
A) Because the master used the word 'free'
B) Because the exclusive phrase 'nothing but' clearly indicates that emancipation is the only intended meaning
C) Because it is a metaphor
D) Because the slave is a mahram

Key Takeaway
The phrase 'ma anta illa hurr' is a clear and binding declaration of emancipation because the exclusive particle 'illa' leaves no doubt about the master's intent.

Partial Emancipation: Abu Hanifa vs. the Two Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on partial emancipation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on partial emancipation, explain the hadith proof, and identify the mufta bihi opinion.

Core Idea
Partial emancipation frees only that portion; the unfreed part remains in slavery with the slave working for its value.

When a master frees only part of his slave, a well-known disagreement arises within the Hanafi school. Imam Abu Hanifa insists that only the explicitly freed portion becomes free, while the rest remains in slavery and the slave must work to earn his remaining value. The two Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that the entire slave becomes free immediately. This lesson unpacks their proofs and the relied-upon ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the two positions
Read the passage carefully: a master frees a portion of his slave. What does Abu Hanifa rule? What do the Sahibayn rule? Write down each position in one sentence.
2
Trace the reasoning of Abu Hanifa
Why does Abu Hanifa limit the emancipation to the freed portion? The passage says: 'because it is the master's property; he can withhold whatever portion he wishes.' Also, a hadith is cited: 'Whoever frees a share of a slave, then only that share is freed.' Identify the principle (qāʿida) behind this reasoning.
3
Understand the Sahibayn's argument
The Sahibayn hold that the entire slave is freed. Though the text does not detail their proof, they likely rely on the same hadith differently or on a different legal analogy. Since this is an intra-Hanafi dispute, you need to know both sides. Infer what their key argument might be: perhaps they consider freedom indivisible, or they emphasize that the hadith requires the master to compensate the partners, implying full freedom.
The source text does not elaborate on the Sahibayn's proof, but later commentaries explain they view the hadith as commanding full freedom when the master can afford it.
4
Examine the hadith cited and its implications
The hadith from Abdullah ibn Umar says: 'Whoever frees a share of a slave, and he has wealth that reaches the price of the slave, then the slave is valued and he gives [the partners their shares].' The passage uses this to support Abu Hanifa: only the freed share is freed, and the slave works to pay the value. What does 'saʿy' (seeking) mean here? How does it differ from the Sahibayn's interpretation?
5
Identify the mufta bihi and why
The text states that the position of Abu Hanifa is relied upon. Why? Because the hadith directly supports it, and it aligns with the principle that property rights are respected. Conclude by stating the practical ruling: the slave is partially free and must work to purchase the remaining portion.
This is a clear example of tarjih based on textual evidence (dalīl) over qiyas.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۲۰۲] (۱۳) اور اگر آقا نے اپنے بعض غلام کو آزاد کیا تو یہ بعض حصہ آزاد ہو جائے گا اور بقیہ قیمت میں مولی کے لئے سعی کرے گا۔ اور صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ کل آزاد ہو گا۔
پورا غلام آقا ہی کا تھا۔ اب آقا نے اس کا بعض حصہ آزاد کیا تو یہ بعض ہی آزاد ہوگا۔ امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک کل آزاد نہیں ہوگا ۔ اور صاحبین کے نزدیک کل غلام آزاد ہو جائے گا۔
امام ابو حنیفہ کا قاعدہ یہ ہے کہ آقا نے جتنا غلام آزاد کیا اتناہی آزاد ہوگا اور جتنا حصہ آزاد نہیں کیا اتنا حصہ غلامیت میں رہے گا۔ کیونکہ آقا کی چیز ہے اس لئے جتنا حصہ روکنا چاہے وہ روک سکتا ہے (۲) حدیث میں ہے کہ جتنا حصہ آزاد کرے گا اتنا ہی آزاد ہوگا۔ عن عبد اللہ بن عمر ان رسول الله الا الله قال من اعتق شركا له في عبد فكان له مال يبلغ ثمن العبد قوم العبد عليه قيمة عدل فاعطى
[2202] (13) And if the master frees a part of his slave, then that part is freed, and he (the slave) will work (seek) for the remaining value for his master. And the two (Sahibayn) say that the whole is freed. The entire slave belonged to the master. Now if the master frees a part of him, only that part is freed. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the whole is not freed. According to the two Sahibayn, the entire slave will be freed. The principle of Imam Abu Hanifa is that as much of the slave as the master frees, that much is freed, and the portion he did not free remains in slavery, because it is the master's property; he can withhold whatever portion he wishes. (2) There is a hadith that as much as he frees, that much is freed. From Abdullah ibn Umar that the Messenger of Allah peace be upon him said: 'Whoever frees a share of a slave, and he has wealth that reaches the price of the slave, then the slave is valued with a just valuation and he gives [the partners their shares].'
Source pages p. 244

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding partial emancipation. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that only the portion explicitly freed becomes free; the rest remains in slavery, and the slave must work (sa'y) to earn the value of the remaining portion for the master. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that the entire slave becomes free immediately upon partial emancipation, based on the hadith of Abdullah ibn Umar which implies that freeing a share leads to full emancipation if the master has wealth to compensate the remaining shares. However, the text presents Abu Hanifa's principle: a master can free only what he wishes, as it is his property. The hadith cited supports Abu Hanifa: only the freed portion is free, and the slave works to pay for the remainder.

Key Terms
سعی (sa'y): The slave's effort to earn money to pay the remaining value of himself to the master after partial emancipation.
عتاق (itq): Emancipation, freeing of a slave.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, what happens to the part of a slave that the master did not free?
A) It becomes automatically free
B) It remains in slavery, and the slave works to pay its value
C) The master must free it later
D) The slave is sold

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, partial emancipation frees only the specified portion; the remainder stays in slavery with the slave obligated to earn its value for the master.

Automatic Manumission of a Mahram Relative
States ruling and provides hadith proof for freeing a mahram relative upon ownership

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that owning a mahram relative automatically frees the slave, and identify the hadith proof and its legal implication.

Core Idea
Ownership of a mahram relative automatically frees them — the slave becomes free by the mere fact of ownership.

This lesson presents a ruling with its proof: if a person owns a close relative whom he cannot marry (a mahram), the slave is automatically freed. This is based on a hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him). The commentary explains that such ownership is not commendable, hence the immediate manumission. We will examine the ruling, its conditions, and the evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? The act of owning a mahram relative. The ruling is that the relative becomes free automatically.
The ruling is a consequence, not a voluntary act.
2
Locate the dalil
What proof is cited? A hadith from Samura ibn Jundub (as reported by Hammad) that the Prophet said: 'Whoever owns a mahram relative, he becomes free.'
The hadith is from Abu Dawud and Tirmidhi.
3
Analyse the wajh al-dalalah
How does the hadith prove the ruling? The phrase 'فهو حر' (he is free) is a declarative sentence indicating immediate freedom. In Hanafi usul, such a statement in a legal context is taken as a command (wujub).
The dalala is qati (definitive) in meaning, though thubut is zanni (ahad hadith).
4
Identify the condition
What is required for this ruling? The relative must be a mahram (within prohibited degrees). Non-mahram relatives (e.g., cousins) are not included.
The term 'dhu rahm mahram' is key.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا ملك الرجل ذارحم محرم منه عتق عليه [۲۲۰۱] (۱۲) اگر آدمی ذی رحم محرم کا مالک ہو جائے تو وہ اس پر آزاد ہو جائے گا۔ ذی رحم محرم جیسے قریبی رشتہ والے کا مالک ہو اور اس کو غلام بنا کر رکھے ایسا اچھا معلوم نہیں ہوتا۔ اس لئے وہ آزاد ہو جائے گا (۲) حدیث میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ عن سمرة بن جندب فيما يحسب حماد قال قال رسول الله الله من ملك ذا رحم محرم فهو حر (الف) (ابوداؤد شریف ، باب فیمن ملک زار تم محرم، ص ۱۹۴ نمبر ۳۹۴۹ / ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء فیمن ملک زار تم محرم ، ص ۲۵۳ نمبر ۱۳۶۵) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ ذی رحم محرم کا مالک ہوا تو وہ آزاد ہو جائے گا۔
If a man owns a dhi rahm mahram (a close relative prohibited in marriage), that relative becomes free upon him.
Source pages p. 244

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof. The commentator states that owning a close relative (like a parent, child, sibling) is not commendable, and thus the slave is freed. The proof is a hadith from Samura ibn Jundub (as reported by Hammad) that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever owns a dhi rahm mahram, he becomes free.' The hadith is from Abu Dawud and Tirmidhi. The ruling is thus established: ownership of a mahram relative automatically results in manumission.

Key Terms
ذو رحم محرم (dhu rahm mahram): A close blood relative whom one cannot marry, such as parents, children, siblings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Based on the hadith, if a man owns his brother as a slave, what is the ruling?
A) The brother remains a slave.
B) The brother becomes free automatically.
C) The brother is freed only if the owner declares it.
D) The brother must serve for six years before freedom.

Key Takeaway
Owning a mahram relative automatically frees them, based on the hadith of Samura ibn Jundub.

Freeing Part of a Slave: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
A textual expansion probing an intra-Hanafi dispute with dalil naqli.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on partial manumission, identify their respective proofs, and explain the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
Manumission divisibility splits Hanafi imams: partial freedom vs. the whole slave freed.

This passage presents an important intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf concerning the effect of freeing part of a slave. The ruling has practical consequences for when the slave achieves full freedom. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to trace ikhtilaf to its usul roots—here, the principle of divisibility (tajazzi) of acts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
Read the passage and note what Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn hold. Abu Hanifa: only the freed portion becomes free. Sahibayn: the entire slave becomes free.
The passage explicitly states 'Abu Hanifa says only that part is free; the two companions say the whole is free.'
2
Locate each side's dalil
Find the hadiths cited for each view. For Abu Hanifa: hadith of Ibn Umar and the story of Tahman/Dhakwan. For Sahibayn: hadith of Abu Huraira and hadith of Abu al-Malih.
Pay attention to how each hadith is used to support the respective principle of divisibility or indivisibility.
3
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf
Determine the practical difference: if a master frees half, under Abu Hanifa only half is free and the slave works for the other half; under Sahibayn the whole is free immediately and the slave works for the entire value. The timing of full freedom differs.
This affects inheritance, marriage, and other rulings dependent on slave status.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
Later Hanafi authorities (e.g., al-Hidayah, al-Durr al-Mukhtar) prefer the Sahibayn's view. The passage indicates the relied-upon position is that the entire slave becomes free.
The commentator does not explicitly give tarjih, but the mufta bihi is the Sahibayn's view in later fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا اعتق المولى بعض عبده عتق عليه ذلك البعض ويسعى في بقية قيمته لمولاه [۲۲۰۲] (۱۳) اور اگر آقا نے اپنے بعض غلام کو آزاد کیا تو یہ بعض حصہ آزاد ہو جائے گا اور بقیہ قیمت میں مولی کے لئے سعی کرے گا۔ اور صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ کل آزاد ہو گا۔ پورا غلام آقا ہی کا تھا۔ اب آقا نے اس کا بعض حصہ آزاد کیا تو یہ بعض ہی آزاد ہوگا۔ امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک کل آزاد نہیں ہوگا ۔ اور صاحبین کے نزدیک کل غلام آزاد ہو جائے گا۔ امام ابو حنیفہ کا قاعدہ یہ ہے کہ آقا نے جتنا غلام آزاد کیا اتناہی آزاد ہوگا اور جتنا حصہ آزاد نہیں کیا اتنا حصہ غلامیت میں رہے گا۔ کیونکہ آقا کی چیز ہے اس لئے جتنا حصہ روکنا چاہے وہ روک سکتا ہے (۲) حدیث میں ہے کہ جتنا حصہ آزاد کرے گا اتنا ہی آزاد ہوگا۔ عن عبد اللہ بن عمر ان رسول الله الا الله قال من اعتق شركا له في عبد فكان له مال يبلغ ثمن العبد قوم العبد عليه قيمة عدل فاعطى حاشیہ : (الف) آپ نے فرمایا جوزی رحم محرم کا مالک ہو تو وہ آزاد ہو جائے گا۔  الشرح الثميرى الجزء الثالث) ۲۴۰ كتاب العتاق عند ابي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى وقالا يعتق كله. شركاءه حصصهم وعتق عليه العبد والا فقد عتق منه ما عتق (الف) ( بخاری شریف، باب اذا اعتق عبد امین اثنین ادامه بین الشرکا ص۳۲۲ نمبر ۲۵۲۲، مسلم شریف ، باب من اعتق شرکاء لہ فی عبد ص ۴۹۱ نمبر (۱۵۰) اس حدیث میں یہ ہے کہ اگر آزاد کرنے والے کے پاس باقی غلام کی قیمت نہ ہو تو اتنا ہی آزاد ہوگا جتنا آزاد ہوا۔ اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ غلام کی آزادگی میں حصہ اور تجزی ہو سکتا ہے۔ اس لئے آقا نے جتنا آزاد کیا اتنا ہی آزاد ہوگا۔ اور اپنا باقی حصہ غلام سعی کر کے آقا کو ادا کرے گا (۲) حدیث میں ہے۔ حدثنی اسمعیل بن امیه عن ابيه عن جده قال كان لهم غلام يقال له طهمان او ذكوان قال فاعتق جده نصفه فجاء العبد إلى النبي الله فاخبره فقال النبى الله تعتق في عتقك وترق في رقك قال فكان يخدم سيده حتى مات (ب) (سنن بی لليبقى ، باب من اعتق من مملو که شقصاج عاشر ص ۴۶۳ نمبر ۲۱۳۱۹ ، مصنف عبد الرزاق، باب من اعتق بعض عبده ج تاسع ص ۱۴۹ نمبر ۱۶۷۰۵) اس حدیث سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ جتنا آزاد کیا اتنا ہی آزاد ہوگا۔ صاحبین کے نزدیک پورا غلام آزاد ہوگا۔ یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن ابي هريرة ان النبى الله قال من اعتق نصيبا او شقصا في مملوک فخلاصة عليه في ماله ان كان له مال والا قوم عليه فاستشعی به غیر مشفوق علیه (ج) ( بخاری شریف ، باب اذا اعتق نصیبانی عبدولیس لہ مال استعی العبد غير مشقوق علیه ص ۳۴۳ نمبر ۲۵۲۷، مسلم شریف ، باب ذکر سعایۃ العبد ص ۴۹۱ نمبر ۱۵۰۳) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ اگر آزاد کرنے والے شریک کے پاس باقی غلام کی قیمت نہ ہو تب بھی پورا غلام آزاد ہوگا اور غلام کو اپنی قیمت سعی کر کے ادا کرنا ہوگا۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ آدھا آزاد کرنے سے پورا غلام آزاد ہوگا۔ آزادگی میں تجری نہیں ہوگی (۲) عن ابی المليح ان رجلا من قومه اعتق ثلث غلامه فرفع ذلك الى النبي الالالا لاله فقال هو حر كله ليس لله شریک (و) (سن للبیهقی ، باب من احق من مملو که شقصاج عاشر ص ۲۷۴ نمبر ۲۱۳۱۷، مصنف عبدالرزاق ، باب من الحق بعض عبده ج تاسع ص ۱۴۹ نمبر ۱۶۷۰۸) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا پورا غلام آزاد ہوگا ۔ اصول امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک جتنا غلام آزاد کیا اتنا ہی حصہ آزاد ہوگا باقی غلام باقی رہے گا۔ صاحبین کے نزدیک آزادگی میں تجری نہیں ہے اس لئے پورا غلام آزاد ہوگا۔
If the master frees part of his slave, that part becomes free, and the slave works for the remaining value for his master. Abu Hanifa says only that part is free; the two companions say the whole is free.
Source pages p. 244

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute. The text presents the ruling that if a master frees a portion of his slave, that portion becomes free and the slave must work to compensate the master for the remaining value. Then the dispute is introduced: Imam Abu Hanifa holds that only the freed portion becomes free, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) hold that the entire slave becomes free. The commentator provides supporting hadith for both sides. For Abu Hanifa, the hadith of Ibn Umar is cited: 'Whoever frees a share in a slave... then only that which is freed is freed.' Also the story of Tahman/Dhakwan where the Prophet said: 'You are free in your freed part, and a slave in your enslaved part.' For the Sahibayn, the hadith of Abu Huraira is cited: 'Whoever frees a portion of a slave, he is fully free if he has wealth; otherwise he is valued and the slave works without hardship.' Also the hadith of Abu al-Malih: 'He is fully free; Allah has no partner.' The commentator concludes by stating the principle: for Abu Hanifa, manumission is divisible; for the Sahibayn, it is not divisible, so partial manumission frees the entire slave. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the Hanafi school is that of the Sahibayn, as indicated by later authorities.

Key Terms
سعی (sa'aya): The slave works (earning money) to pay the master for the unfreed portion's value.
تجزی (tajazzi): Divisibility; whether manumission can take effect in parts.
شقص (shiqs): A share or portion, used in hadiths to describe freeing a portion of a slave.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school, if a master frees half of his slave, what is the ruling?
A) Only half becomes free; the slave works for the other half.
B) The entire slave becomes free and must work to pay half the value.
C) The entire slave becomes free and owes nothing.
D) The freeing is invalid because it is partial.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the relied-upon position is that partial manumission frees the entire slave (Sahibayn's view), reversing the earlier ruling of Abu Hanifa.

8 min
Partner's Recourse When Co-owner Frees His Share: Abu Hanifa vs Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute with hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the partner's recourse when a co-owner frees his share and the co-owner is insolvent, and state the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
When a co-owner frees his share, the partner's recourse depends on the co-owner's wealth: claim from him if affluent, otherwise the slave works.

This lesson examines the intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two pupils, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, regarding the legal consequences when one co-owner frees his share of a jointly-owned slave and the co-owner lacks wealth. The central question is whether the partner can compel the slave to work (sa'yah) to compensate his share or must seek payment from the co-owner. Understanding this dispute reveals important principles about the indivisibility of freedom and the application of hadith proofs.

Guided Path
1
State the Problem
Identify the scenario: a jointly-owned slave, one co-owner frees his share, the co-owner is insolvent. What recourse does the partner have to recover the value of his share?
The partner's share is now owned by the freed portion, but the slave is not fully free unless compensated.
2
Identify the Two Hanafi Positions
Abu Hanifa holds that the slave must work (sa'yah) to pay the partner's share regardless of the co-owner's wealth. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) differentiate: if the co-owner is affluent, the partner must claim from him; only if insolvent does the slave work.
Abu Hanifa views the hadith of Abu Hurairah as general; Sahibayn rely on the hadith of Ibn Umar and the principle that freedom is indivisible.
3
Analyze Abu Hanifa's Proof
The hadith of Abu Hurairah states: 'Whoever frees a share in a slave... if he has no wealth, he is valued and the slave works without hardship.' Abu Hanifa takes this as the default rule: the slave works even if the co-owner is wealthy? Actually, the hadith only mentions the case of no wealth. But Abu Hanifa applies it generally.
The other hadith (Ibn Umar) is interpreted by Abu Hanifa as conditional on the co-owner paying; if he doesn't, the slave works.
4
Analyze the Sahibayn's Proof
The hadith of Ibn Umar states: 'Whoever frees a share in a slave, then the whole slave is freed if he has enough wealth; otherwise, only his share becomes free.' This implies that if the co-owner is affluent, the partner must seek payment from him, not from the slave. Freedom is indivisible, so the entire slave becomes free upon the co-owner's act, and the partner's claim is against the co-owner.
The Sahibayn also cite the principle 'ghayr mashquq alayh' (without hardship) to support making the slave work only when necessary.
5
Determine the Thamarah al-Khilaf and the Mufta Bihi
The practical difference: According to Abu Hanifa, the partner cannot demand payment from the co-owner's other wealth if he is insolvent; only the slave's work is available. According to the Sahibayn, the partner must demand from the co-owner if he is affluent. The mufta bihi is the Sahibayn's view, as it avoids hardship on the slave and is consistent with the hadith of Ibn Umar.
Al-Marghinani in Al-Hidayah and later fatwa collections prefer the Sahibayn's view.

Source Text

اس پر ڈالنے سے کوئی فائدہ نہیں ہے (٢) حدیث میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ عن ابی هريرة أن النبى الله قال من اعتق نصيبا او شقصا في مملوک فخلاصه عليه في ماله ان كان له مال والا قوم عليه فاستسعی به غیر مشقوق عليه (الف) ( بخاری شریف، باب اذا احتق نصیبان عبد ولیس له مال استسعى العبد غیر مشقوق علیه ص ٣٤٣ نمبر ٢٥٢٧، مسلم شریف ، باب ذکر سعایۃ العبد ص ٤٩١ نمبر ١٥٠٣) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ آزاد کرنے والا مالدار نہ ہو تو غلام اپنی قیمت کی سعایت کرے گا۔ یہ امام ابو حنیفہ کی رائے ہے۔ [٢٢٠٥] (١٦) اور امام ابو یوسف اور محمد نے فرمایا کہ شریک کے لئے نہیں ہے مگر تاوان مالداری کی صورت میں اور سعایت تنگ دستی کی صورت میں ر صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر آزاد کرنے والا مالدار ہے تو شریک کو ایک ہی اختیار ہے کہ مالدار سے اپنے حصے کی قیمت لے لے۔ اس صورت میں غلام سے سعایت کرانے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے۔ ان کے اصول کے مطابق آزاد کرنے والے کے آزاد کرتے ہی پورا غلام آزاد ہو گیا۔ کیونکہ ان کے یہاں آزادگی میں تجزی اور ٹکڑا پن نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے گویا کہ پورا غلام آزاد کرنے والے کی جانب سے آزاد ہو گیا۔ اس لئے شریک کے لئے ایک ہی اختیار ہے کہ آزاد کرنے والے سے اپنے حصے کی قیمت وصول کرے (٢) حدیث میں ہے۔ عن ابن عمر قال قال رسول الله الله من اعتق شركا له في مملوک فعليه عتقه كله ان كان له مال يبلغ ثمنه فان لم يكن له مال يقوم عليه قيمة عدل على المعتق فاعتق منه ما اعتق (ب) ( بخاری شریف، باب اذا اعتق عبدا بین اثنین اوامته بین الشر کا ص ٣٤٣ نمبر ٢٥٢٣، مسلم شریف ، باب من الحق شر کاله فی عبد ص ٤٩١ نمبر ١٥٠١) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ اگر آزاد کرنے والے کے پاس مال ہو تو اس سے اپنے حصے کا تاوان وصول کر لے گا۔ اور اگر آزاد کرنے والا تنگ دست ہو تو غلام سے سعایت کرائے گا۔ اس کی دلیل اوپر کی حدیث والا قوم عليه فاستسعی به غیر مشقوق عليه (ج) ( بخاری شریف، نمبر ٢٥٢٧، مسلم شریف نمبر ١٥٠٣) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ آزاد کرنے والا تنگ دست ہو تو غلام سے سعایت کرالے۔ حاشیہ : (الف) آپ نے فرمایا ملک میں سے جس نے اپنا حصہ آزاد کیا تو اس کے مال سے اس کا چھٹکارا دلانا ضروری ہے اگر اس کے پاس مال ہے۔ اور اگر مال نہیں ہے تو اس کی قیمت لگائی جائے گی۔ غلام اس کی سعایت کرے گا جو اس پر مشقت نہ ہو ( ب ) آپ نے فرمایا جس نے مملوک میں شرکت والے حصے کو آزاد کیا تو اس پر آزاد کرتا ہے اگر اس کے پاس اتنا مال ہو جو قیمت کو پہنچ سکے۔ اور اگر مال نہ ہو تو آزاد کرنے والے پر انصاف والی قیمت لگائی جائے، اور جتنا آزاد کیا اتنا ہی آزاد ہوگا (ج) اگر آزاد کرنے والے کے پاس مال نہ ہو تو غلام سعایت کرے گا تا کہ اس پر مشقت نہ ہو۔
The slave works (sa'yah) and this according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him. 2205 (12) And Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on them both, said: He has nothing except guaranty with affluence and sa'yah in case of insolvency. The one who frees the slave has no wealth, so there is no benefit in imposing the partner's share's price on him. (2) There is proof of this in a hadith: from Abu Hurairah that the Prophet, peace be upon him, said: Whoever frees a share or a portion in a slave, then his full emancipation is upon him from his wealth if he has wealth; otherwise, he is valued and the slave works for it without hardship. (al-Bukhari, Muslim) From this hadith it is understood that if the one who frees is not wealthy, the slave works for his price. This is the view of Imam Abu Hanifa. [2205] (16) And Imam Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: The partner has nothing except compensation in case of affluence and sa'yah in case of insolvency. The two masters (Sahibayn) say: If the one who frees is wealthy, the partner has only one option: to take the price of his share from the wealthy one. In that case, there is no need to make the slave work. According to their principles, as soon as the one who frees frees, the entire slave becomes free, because in their view there is no divisibility in freedom. So it is as if the entire slave is freed by the one who freed; therefore the partner has only one option: to collect the price of his share from the one who freed. (2) There is a hadith: from Ibn Umar, he said: The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said: Whoever frees a share of his in a slave, then the freedom of the whole slave is upon him if he has wealth reaching its price; if he does not have wealth, then a fair price is valued upon the liberator, and only that which he freed becomes free. (al-Bukhari, Muslim) From this hadith it is understood that if the one who frees has wealth, he will collect the compensation for his share from him; and if the one who frees is insolvent, he will make the slave work. Its proof is the previous hadith: 'he is valued and the slave works without hardship.' (al-Bukhari, Muslim) In this hadith, it is that if the one who frees is insolvent, the slave works. Footnote: (a) He said: Whoever frees his share in property, then it is necessary to secure his release from his wealth if he has wealth; if he does not have wealth, then a price is placed on him, and the slave works for it without hardship. (b) He said: Whoever frees a share in a slave, then the rest of the slave becomes free if he has enough wealth to cover the price; if he does not have wealth, then a fair price is placed on the liberator, and only what he freed becomes free. (c) If the one who frees does not have wealth, then the slave will work so that there is no hardship on him.
Source pages p. 247

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two companions, Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), regarding the legal effect when a co-owner frees his share of a jointly-owned slave and the co-owner is insolvent. The core issue is whether the partner can only claim the value from the co-owner (if affluent) or can also have the slave work (sa'yah) to pay off the debt. Abu Hanifa, relying on the hadith of Abu Hurairah, holds that if the co-owner is insolvent, the slave must work to compensate the partner for his share. The Sahibayn distinguish: if the co-owner is affluent, the partner must take the price from him; only if the co-owner is insolvent does the slave work. Their reasoning is based on the principle that freedom is not divisible: once a co-owner frees his share, the entire slave becomes free, so the partner's claim is solely against the co-owner, not the slave. The hadith of Ibn Umar supports the Sahibayn's view, stating that if the co-owner has wealth, the whole slave is freed; otherwise only the freed share is free. The commentary explains both proofs and the hashya provides further clarification of the hadith terms.

Key Terms
سعاية (sa'yah): The slave working to earn money to pay off the debt of his value to the partner
ضمان (daman): Liability or guarantee; here refers to the partner's claim for the price of his share

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi (Sahibayn), what is the partner's recourse when the co-owner is affluent?
A) The slave must work to pay the partner's share.
B) The partner must claim the price from the co-owner.
C) The partner has no recourse; the slave is fully free.
D) The partner can choose between claiming from co-owner or making the slave work.

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi is the Sahibayn's view: the partner's recourse depends on the co-owner's wealth—claim from him if affluent, else the slave works.

Automatic Freedom of a Mahram Relative and the Partner's Option
Ruling on automatic freedom of father's share when buying his son, and partner's options.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Abu Hanifa holds no liability for the father when his share is automatically freed, and evaluate the Sahibayn's counter-argument based on causation.

Core Idea
Owning a mahram relative automatically frees the slave, but intentional causation may create liability.

This passage from al-Sharh al-Sameri examines a scenario where two people jointly buy a slave who turns out to be the son of one partner. According to Hanafi law, simply owning a close relative like a son automatically frees that share. But does the father have to compensate his partner for the lost share? A well-known intra-madhhab dispute arises between Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What happens when a person buys his own son? The son's share is freed automatically without any manumission act.
The key is automatic freedom vs. intentional freeing.
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith 'Whoever owns a mahram relative becomes free' is the evidence. Identify its source and chain.
This is a specific Hanafi proof; other schools may not accept it.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'huwa hurr' indicates that freedom is an immediate legal consequence of ownership; no separate intention is required.
Hanafi usul: the imperative or declarative statement is taken at face value.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Abu Hanifa says no liability on father in both purchase and inheritance. The Sahibayn distinguish: liability in purchase because the father knew the consequence.
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute based on causation vs. automaticity.
5
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf
According to Abu Hanifa, the partner cannot claim from the father; according to Sahibayn, the partner can claim from the father in purchase.
The mufta bihi is the Sahibayn's view for precaution.

(۲۰) واذا اشترى رجلان ابن احدهما عتق نصيب الاب ولا ضمان عليه وكذلك اذا ورثاه والشريك بالخيار ان شاء اعتق نصيبه وان شاء استسعى العبد ۲۰ (۱) واذا شهد كل واحد من الشر يكين على الآخر بالحرية سعى العبد لكل [۲۲۰۶) (۱۷) اگر دو آدمیوں نے ان میں سے ایک کے بیٹے کو خریدا تو باپ کا حصہ آزاد ہو جائے گا۔ اور باپ پر ضمان نہیں ہے۔ ایسے ہی اگر غلام کے وارث ہوئے ہوں۔ پس شریک کو اختیار ہے چاہے اپنا حصہ آزاد کر دے اور چاہے تو غلام سے سعایت کرالے۔ ر دو آدمیوں نے مل کر ایک غلام خریدا جو ان دو آدمیوں میں سے ایک کا بیٹا تھا۔ چونکہ وہ اپنے بیٹے کے آدھے حصے کا مالک بنا اس لئے حديث من ملك ذا رحم محرم فهو حر (ابوداؤد شریف، نمبر ۳۹۴۹، ترمذی شریف، نمبر ۱۳۶۵) کی وجہ سے غلام کا آدھا حصہ جو باپ کا تھا آزاد ہو گیا تو اس صورت میں دوسرا شریک باپ سے اپنے حصے کا ضمان نہیں لے سکتا ہے۔ باپ نے خود آزاد نہیں کیا بلکہ ذی رحم کے مالک ہونے کی وجہ سے خود بخود آزاد ہوا ہے۔ تو چونکہ باپ کی غلطی نہیں ہے اس لئے اس سے ضمان نہیں لے گا۔ اب یا تو شریک اپنا حصہ آزاد کرے یا پھر غلام سے سعایت کرالے (۲) حدیث میں اس کا اشارہ ہے۔ عن سالم عن ابيه عن النبي الله الله قال من اعتق عبدا بين اثنين فان كان موسرا قوم عليه ثم يعتق (الف) بخاری شریف، باب اذا اعتق عبدا بین اثنین ادامه بین الشر کا ص ۱۳۴۳ نمبر ۲۵۲۱، مسلم شریف ، باب من احتق شر کالہ فی عبد ص ۴۲۹۱ نمبر (۱۵۰) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ آزاد کیا ہو تو اس پر ضمان ہو گا۔ یہاں آزاد کیا نہیں بلکہ قرابت کی وجہ سے خود بخود آزاد ہو گیا اس لئے باپ پر ضمان لازم نہیں ہوگا۔ اسی طرح ایک آدمی نے غلام خرید ابعد میں اس کے آدھے حصہ کا رشتہ دار وارث بن گیا جس کی وجہ سے اس کا آدھا حصہ آزاد ہو گیا تو شریک اپنے حصے کی قیمت اس وارث سے وصول نہیں کر سکتا۔ کیونکہ وارث نے جان بوجھ کر آزاد نہیں کیا ہے بلکہ موت کی وجہ سے خود بخود وارث ہوا اور ذی رحم محرم کے مالک ہونے کی وجہ سے خود بخود آزاد بھی ہو گیا۔ اس لئے اس کی کوئی غلطی نہیں ہے۔ صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ وارث ہونے کی شکل میں تو وارث ضامن نہیں ہوگا لیکن باپ کے خریدنے کی شکل میں باپ شریک کے حصے کا ضامن ہوگا۔ باپ جانتا تھا کہ میرے خریدنے سے بیٹا آزاد ہوگا۔ اس کے باوجود اپنے بیٹے کو خریدا تو گویا کہ جان بوجھ کر شریک کو نقصان دیا اس لئے باپ ضامن ہوگا۔
(20) And if two men buy the son of one of them, the father's share is freed and there is no liability upon him, and similarly if they inherit him. And the partner has the option: if he wishes he may free his share, and if he wishes he may make the slave work. 20 (1) And if each of the two partners testifies against the other regarding freedom, the slave works for both. [2206] (17) If two persons buy the son of one of them, the father's share will be freed, and there is no liability on the father. Similarly, if they inherit the slave. Then the partner has the option: if he wishes, he may free his share, and if he wishes, he may take sa'yah from the slave. Two persons jointly bought a slave who was the son of one of them. Since he became the owner of half of his son, due to the hadith 'Whoever owns a mahram relative becomes free' (Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi), half the slave which belonged to the father became free. So in this case, the other partner cannot claim liability from the father for his share. The father did not free him himself; rather, due to owning a mahram relative, the slave became automatically free. So since the father is not at fault, he will not be liable. Now the partner may free his share or take sa'yah from the slave. (2) There is an indication of this in a hadith: from Salim from his father from the Prophet, peace be upon him, who said: Whoever frees a slave between two persons, if he is affluent, a value is placed on him then the slave is freed. (Bukhari, Muslim) In this hadith it is that if he freed, liability is upon him. Here he did not free, but due to kinship the slave became free automatically, so liability is not necessary on the father. Similarly, a person bought a slave, and later a relative of half the share became his heir, due to which half of his share was freed. So the partner cannot collect the price of his share from that heir, because the heir did not free intentionally, but became heir due to death and became owner of a mahram relative, thus the slave became free automatically. Therefore he is not at fault. The two masters (Sahibayn) say: In the case of inheritance, the heir is not liable, but in the case of the father's purchase, the father is liable for the partner's share. The father knew that by his purchase his son would become free, yet he bought his son, so it is as if he intentionally caused loss to the partner; therefore the father will be liable.
Source pages p. 248

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding automatic freedom when a person buys his son or inherits a relative. The legal principle is that when a person becomes the owner of a close relative (dhi rahim mahram), such as a son, that relative is automatically freed by the mere fact of ownership. This is based on the hadith: 'Whoever owns a mahram relative becomes free.' In the given scenario, two persons jointly own a slave, and one of them is the father; when they buy the slave (or inherit him), the father's share is automatically freed without any intentional act of manumission. Therefore, the father is not liable to the partner for the value of his share, because the freedom occurred without his choice. The partner has two options: either he also frees his share (in which case the slave is fully free and the partner is considered a free-willer), or he can require the slave to work (sa'yah) to earn the value of the partner's share. The hadith of Salim is cited to show that liability applies only when one intentionally frees; here it is automatic. However, the Sahibayn differentiate: if the father intentionally bought his son knowing it would free him, he is considered to have caused the loss, so he must compensate the partner. In the case of inheritance, no one chooses to inherit, so no liability. This has practical implications: according to Abu Hanifa, the father is never liable, while the Sahibayn hold him liable if he purchased his son knowingly.

Key Terms
ذو رحم محرم (dhu rahim muharram): A close blood relative who is permanently prohibited in marriage, like son, brother, father
ضمان (daman): Liability to pay the partner's share value

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn, why is the father liable for the partner's share when he buys his son?
A) Because the father intended to free his son.
B) Because the father knowingly caused the loss to the partner by purchasing his son.
C) Because the father is always responsible for any automatic freedom.
D) Because the hadith of Salim imposes liability on any owner of a relative.

Key Takeaway
The automatic freedom of a mahram relative does not impose liability on the father in Abu Hanifa's view, but the Sahibayn hold him liable if he purchased knowing the consequence; the mufta bihi follows the Sahibayn.

Each Partner Testifies the Other Freed: Slave Works for Both
Ruling on mutual testimony of freedom between partners

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when two partners mutually testify that the other freed his share, and explain the hadith-based analogy that supports it.

Core Idea
Mutual testimony of freedom obligates the slave to work for both partners' shares.

This lesson deals with a specific scenario in Hanafi fiqh: two joint owners of a slave each testify that the other freed his share. Imam Abu Hanifa rules that the slave must work (sa'yah) to earn the value of both shares, regardless of the partners' affluence. The ruling is derived by analogy from the well-known hadith about freeing a jointly-owned slave.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is mutual testimony by two partners that each other freed their share of a jointly-owned slave. The ruling is that the slave must work (sa'yah) to pay the value of both shares.
The ruling applies whether the partners are affluent or insolvent.
2
Locate the condition
The condition is that each partner testifies that the other freed his share. This mutual testimony is treated as evidence that freedom has been effected from both sides.
The condition is not actual manumission but testimony, which is considered a legal cause.
3
Understand the consequence
The slave becomes obligated to work (sa'yah) to compensate both partners for the value of their shares. This work is wajib until the full value is paid.
If one partner merely testifies without reciprocity, this ruling does not apply.
4
Connect to the hadith
The ruling is based on analogy (qiyas) to the hadith: 'Whoever frees a slave between two persons, then if he is affluent, a value is placed on him, then the entire slave is freed.' Mutual testimony is analogous to actual freeing because it indicates the intention to free.
The hadith is cited in the hashya and supports the principle that when freedom is established, the slave must compensate if the owner is not affluent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا شهد كل واحد من الشريكين على الآخر بالحرية سعى العبد لكل (۲۲۰۷) (۱۸) گرد و شریکوں میں سے ہر ایک نے دوسرے پر آزاد کرنے کی گواہی دی تو غلام دونوں میں سے ہر ایک کے لئے ان کے حصوں میں سعایت کرے گا دونوں مالدار ہوں یا تنگ دست امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک ۔ ایک غلام دو آدمیوں کے درمیان تھا مثلا زید کا آدھا حصہ تھا اور خالد کا آدھا حصہ تھا۔ اب زید نے گواہی دی کہ خالد نے اپنا حصہ آزاد حاشیہ : (الف) آپ نے فرمایا جس نے دو آدمیوں کے درمیان غلام کو آزاد کیا۔ پس اگر وہ مالدار ہے تو اس پر قیمت لگائی جائے گی پھر پورا غلام آزاد ہوگا۔
And if each of the two partners testifies against the other regarding freedom, the slave works for both. [2207] (18) If each of the two partners testifies that the other freed, then the slave will work for each of them in their shares, whether both are affluent or insolvent, according to Imam Abu Hanifa. There was a slave between two men: for example, Zayd owned half and Khalid owned half. Then Zayd testified that Khalid freed his share. Footnote: (a) He said: Whoever frees a slave between two persons, then if he is affluent, a value is placed on him, then the entire slave is freed.
Source pages p. 248

Commentary
This passage states a ruling from Imam Abu Hanifa regarding a scenario where two partners in a jointly-owned slave each testify that the other partner freed his share. In such a case, the slave must work (sa'yah) to earn the value of both shares, regardless of whether the partners are affluent or insolvent. The reasoning is that the testimony creates a situation where each partner is considered to have caused the freedom of the other's share, so the slave owes the value to both. The hashya clarifies that if one partner actually frees the slave, the ruling is different: if he is affluent, the full value is imposed on him and the slave becomes free. The passage is brief but indicates that the sa'yah applies to both shares in this mutual testimony scenario, which is a specific application of the general principle that when freedom occurs without intention, the slave is responsible.

Key Terms
شهادة (shahada): Testimony; here it is a statement by one partner that the other freed his share, which triggers the ruling.
سعاية (sa'yah): Work performed by a slave to earn money to pay for his freedom or to compensate a master.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what is the consequence when each partner testifies that the other freed his share?
A) The slave is immediately freed without any payment.
B) The slave must work to pay both partners' shares.
C) The partners must pay each other from their own wealth.
D) The testimony is ignored and the status quo remains.

Key Takeaway
Mutual testimony of freedom between joint owners obligates the slave to work for both shares, based on analogy to the hadith of freeing a jointly-owned slave.

Sa'y When One Partner Testifies to Another's Emancipation
Intra-Hanafi dispute on sa'y after testimony of emancipation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state Abu Hanifa's and the Sahibayn's positions on sa'y when one partner testifies against another, and explain the proof and practical difference.

Core Idea
Denial blocks ğamān, so sa'y becomes the slave's path to freedom — but the Sahibayn differentiate by wealth.

When two partners jointly own a slave and one testifies that the other has freed his share, a dispute arises: must the slave perform sa'y (work to compensate) for both partners? Abu Hanifa says yes, always. The Sahibayn distinguish based on whether the alleged emancipator is wealthy. This lesson dissects the proofs and logic behind each view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the dispute
Understand the exact facts: two partners own a slave; one partner testifies that the other freed his share; the other denies. The slave becomes free upon the testimony? The issue is whether sa'y is due and to whom.
The slave is free because the testimony proves the freeing of one share, and the other share follows by istihsān? Actually, the text implies the slave is free, but sa'y is required for compensation.
2
Recall Abu Hanifa's position and its proof
Abu Hanifa holds that the slave performs sa'y for both partners, regardless of their wealth. His proof is an athar from Hamād and the principle that the denying partner cannot be forced to pay ğamān.
The athar: 'If the one against whom testimony is given is wealthy, the slave performs sa'y for him; if he is poor, he performs sa'y for both.' Abu Hanifa interprets this literally: sa'y for both when the accused is poor.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and its logic
The Sahibayn differentiate: if the accused is wealthy, he must pay compensation (ğamān) so no sa'y; if poor, sa'y for both. If one wealthy and one poor, sa'y only for the wealthy.
Their basis: the wealthy partner can afford to pay, so the slave should not be burdened; the poor partner cannot pay, so sa'y falls on the slave.
4
Analyse the refutation and evidence
The text presents Abu Hanifa's response: the athar does not differentiate based on wealth; also, denial prevents imposing ğamān, so sa'y is necessary in both cases.
The commentary adds that the slave becomes like a mukātib, earning his freedom by working for both masters.
5
Extract the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical difference: under Abu Hanifa, the slave always works for both; under the Sahibayn, if the accused is wealthy, the slave does not work for either, or only for the wealthy if the poor partner testified.
This affects the slave's workload and financial burden.

Source Text

واحد منهما في نصيبه موسرین کانا او معسرين عند ابي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى [2208] (19) وقالا ان كانا معسرين سعى لهما [2209 (20) واذا كانا موسرين فلا سعاية وان کر دیا ہے اور خالد نے گواہی دی کہ زید نے اپنا آدھا حصہ آزاد کر دیا ہے تو پورا غلام آزاد ہو جائے گا۔ اور زید کے حصے کی بھی سعایت کرے گا اور خالد کے حصے کے بھی سعایت کرے گا۔ چاہے دونوں مالدار ہوں یا تنگدست ہوں۔ جب زید کہ رہا ہے کہ خالد کا حصہ آزاد ہے اور وہ انکار کر رہا ہے تو زید کے ذہن میں ہے کہ خالد کا حصہ آزاد ہو گیا لیکن وہ انکار کر رہا ہے اس لئے زید خالد سے ضمان نہیں لے سکے گا تو آخری درجہ یہی رہ گیا کہ غلام سے سعایت کر والے یا اپنا حصہ بھی آزاد کر دے۔ یہی حال خالد کا بھی ہے کہ وہ گواہی دے رہا ہے کہ زید نے اپنا حصہ آزاد کر دیا ہے اور وہ انکار کر رہا ہے۔ اس لئے خالد کے ذہن میں ہے کہ زید کا حصہ آزاد ہو گیا لیکن زید پر ضمان نہیں ڈال سکتا کیونکہ وہ انکار کر رہا ہے۔ اس لئے یہی صورت باقی رہ گئی کہ غلام سے سعایت کر والے ۔ اور گویا کہ غلام مکاتب بن گیا اور مکاتب غلام کا آقا مالدار ہو یا تنگ دست دونوں آقاؤں کو مال کتابت کما کر ادا کرتا ہے۔ اس لئے یہاں بھی آقا کو سعایت کر کے دے گا چاہے دونوں آقا مالدار ہو یا تنگدست ۔ اثر میں ہے۔ عن حماد فی عبد بین رجیلین شهد احدهما على الآخر انه اعتقه وانكر الآخر قال ان كان الشهود عليه موسرا سعى له العبد وان كان معسرا سعى لهما جميعا (الف) (مصنف عبد الرزاق، باب العبد بين الرجلين يشهد احدهما على الآخر بالعتق ج تاسع بص 66 نمبر 16776)
اصول یہ مسئلہ اس اصول پر ہے کہ شریک کے انکار کی وجہ سے اس پر ضمان لازم نہیں کر سکتا اس لئے آخری صورت یہ ہے کہ سعایت کرائیگا۔ [2208) (19) اور صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر دونوں مالدار ہوں تو کسی کے لئے سعایت نہیں کرے گا۔ اور اگر دونوں تنگدست ہوں تو دونوں کے لئے سعایت کرے گا۔

(2209] (20) اور اگر دونوں میں سے ایک مالدار ہو اور دوسرا تنگدست ہو تو مالدار کے لئے سعی کرے گا اور تنگ دست کے لئے سعی نہیں کریگا۔ مالدار نے جب کہا کہ تنگدست نے آزاد کیا تو گویا کہ اس نے کہا کہ غلام پر سعایت ہے۔ کیونکہ تنگ دست آزاد کرے تو غلام پر سعایت ہے تنگ دست پر ضمان نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے خود مالدار کے لئے سعایت کرے گا۔ اور تنگ دست نے جب کہا کہ مالدار نے آزاد کیا ہے تو گویا حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت حماد سے روایت ہے کہ ایک غلام دو آدمیوں کے درمیان ہو۔ ایک نے دوسرے پر گواہی دی کہ اس نے آزاد کر دیا اور دوسرے نے انکار کردیا۔ فرمایا کہ مشہود علیہ مالدار ہو تو غلام اس کے لئے سعایت کرے گا اور اگر تنگدست ہو تو دونوں کے لئے سعایت کرے گا۔

Book of Emancipation. One of them in his share, whether they are wealthy or poor, according to Abu Hanifa. (19) And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: If both are poor, the slave performs sa'y for both. (20) And if both are wealthy, there is no sa'y. (Then Urdu commentary: explaining the case of Zayd and Khalid: if Zayd says Khalid freed his share and Khalid denies, the slave is fully free and performs sa'y for both, regardless of wealth or poverty. The principle is that the partner cannot be forced to pay guarantee due to denial, so sa'y is the only option. The slave becomes like a mukatib. There is an athar from Hammad: a slave between two men, one testifies against the other that he freed him, the other denies; if the one against whom testimony is given is wealthy, the slave performs sa'y for him; if he is poor, the slave performs sa'y for both. (19) The two (Sahibayn) say: if both are wealthy, no sa'y for anyone; if both are poor, sa'y for both. (20) And if one is wealthy and the other poor, the slave performs sa'y for the wealthy and not for the poor. (Urdu commentary continues. Footnote: From Hammad: if the accused is wealthy, slave performs sa'y for him; if poor, for both.) And (the matn): if one is wealthy and the other poor, he performs sa'y for the wealthy and not for the poor.
Source pages p. 249

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning a scenario where a slave is jointly owned by two partners, and one partner testifies that the other has freed his share, while the other denies. The core issue is whether the slave must perform sa'y (work to compensate the value of his freedom) and to whom. Abu Hanifa holds that the slave performs sa'y for both partners regardless of their financial status. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) differentiate: if both are wealthy, no sa'y (because the partner who allegedly freed must pay compensation); if both are poor, sa'y for both; if one wealthy and one poor, sa'y only for the wealthy. The text supports Abu Hanifa's view with an athar from Hammad, which states that if the one against whom testimony is given is wealthy, the slave performs sa'y for him, and if poor, for both. The commentary explains the underlying principle: since the partner who denies refuses to accept liability, the slave must earn his freedom through sa'y, similar to a mukatib. The dispute here is purely within the Hanafi school; the text does not explicitly state which position is relied upon for fatwa.

Key Terms
سعایت (sa'y): The slave's working for his master(s) to earn money to pay for his freedom or compensation.
موسر (mūsir): Wealthy, possessing nisab or more, financially able to pay compensation.
معسر (mu‘sir): Poor, not having sufficient wealth to pay compensation.
ضمان (ḍamān): Financial guarantee or liability to pay the value of the freed share.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what is the ruling on sa'y when one partner testifies that the other freed his share and the other denies, regardless of their wealth?
A) The slave performs sa'y for both partners.
B) The slave performs sa'y only for the wealthy partner.
C) No sa'y at all; the freed partner pays compensation.
D) The slave is free with no sa'y.

Key Takeaway
Abu Hanifa requires sa'y for both partners regardless of wealth; the Sahibayn differentiate based on the financial status of the accused.

Emancipation is Valid Even with Impermissible Intention
Ruling with proof on validity of emancipation regardless of intention

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the validity of emancipation regardless of the master's intention and explain the legal reasoning using the hadith proof.

Core Idea
Emancipation words make the slave free; corrupt intentions do not undo clear declarations.

This lesson addresses a key point in the Hanafi fiqh of emancipation (itq): the legal effect of clear words overrides hidden intentions. When a master explicitly utters words of freedom, the slave becomes free even if the master intended the emancipation for Shaytan or an idol. The passage explains why the extra words are surplus and cites a hadith where the Prophet accepted such a declaration without further inquiry.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is emancipation (itq) performed by the master. The ruling is that the slave becomes free immediately upon the utterance of explicit words, regardless of whom the master intended the freedom for (Allah, Shaytan, or an idol).
The intention does not affect the validity of the emancipation; it only affects the moral judgment (makruh for impermissible objects).
2
Locate the proof (dalil)
The author cites the hadith of Abu Huraira who said 'I make you witness that he is for Allah' when freeing his slave. The Prophet accepted this as valid emancipation.
The hadith is from Sahih al-Bukhari, showing that even the phrase 'for Allah' is a valid declaration of freedom.
3
Understand the legal reasoning (wajh al-dalalah)
The word 'huwa lillah' (he is for Allah) is a clear declaration of emancipation. The addition of 'for Shaytan' or 'for an idol' does not negate the explicit words of freedom. In Hanafi usul, clear operative words ('sarih') take effect even if accompanied by a contradictory intention.
The principle is that the legal consequence follows the explicit wording, not the hidden intent, except when the wording is ambiguous.
4
Note the ethical dimension
Freeing a slave for Shaytan or an idol is makruh (disliked) because it associates freedom with something forbidden. However, the legal effect (freedom) still occurs. The master may be sinful but the slave is free.
The passage explicitly says such action is 'not good' but the emancipation takes effect.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(2210 (21) ومن اعتق عبده لوجه الله تعالى او للشيطان او للصنم عتق
كسی نے اپنے غلام کو اللہ کے لئے آزاد کیا یا شیطان کے لئے بابت کے لئے آزاد کیا تو آزاد ہو جائے گا۔ اللہ کے لئے آزاد کیا تو آزاد ہو جائے گا۔ اور شیطان کے لئے آزاد کیا تو ایسا کرنا اگر چہ اچھا نہیں ہے بابت کے لئے آزاد کیا تو ایسا کرنا اچھا نہیں ہے لیکن آزادگی واقع ہو جائے گی۔
ان الفاظ میں آزادگی کے الفاظ پائے گئے۔ اس لئے آزاد ہو جائے گا۔ اور شیطان یا بت کے الفاظ اضافی ہیں اور زائد ہیں اس لئے ان سے کوئی فرق نہیں پڑے گا (2) اللہ کے لئے آزاد کرنے کی حدیث یہ ہے۔ لما اقبل ابو هريرة ومعه غلامه وهو يطلب الاسلام فضل احدهما صاحبه بهذا وقال اما انى اشهدك انه لله (الف) ( بخاری شریف، باب اذا قال لعبده ھولله و نوی العشق والاشهاد بالحق ص 1343 نمبر 2532) اس حدیث میں اللہ کے لئے آزاد کیا گیا ہے۔
(2210 (21) And whoever emancipates his slave for the sake of Allah, or for Shaytan, or for the idol, the slave is emancipated. Someone freed his slave for Allah, or for Shaytan, or for an idol, he becomes free. For Allah is good, for Shaytan or an idol is not good, but emancipation takes effect. Because the words of emancipation are present; the additional words (for Shaytan, idol) are surplus and make no difference. The hadith for freeing for Allah: When Abu Huraira came with his slave seeking Islam, one of them lost the other, and he said: 'I make you witness that he is for Allah.' (Bukhari) In this hadith, he freed for Allah.
Source pages p. 250

Commentary
This passage states a ruling on the validity of emancipation when the master expresses an intention that is not purely for Allah's sake. The ruling is that the emancipation is effective regardless of whether the intention is for Allah, Shaytan, or an idol. The commentary explains that the words of emancipation are clear, and the additional phrases are superfluous; thus the legal effect (freedom) is achieved. The author supports this with a hadith from Abu Huraira where he freed a slave 'for Allah', indicating that such expressions are valid. The ruling is straightforward: the mere act of uttering emancipation words, even with a corrupt intention, results in the slave's freedom. This is consistent with the Hanafi principle that the legal consequence follows the explicit wording, not the hidden intent.

Key Terms
لوجه الله تعالى (li wajhi Allah ta'ala): For the sake of Allah, with sincere intention for divine reward.
العتق (al-'itq): Emancipation of a slave, setting him free.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The slave becomes free because the words of emancipation are present.
C) The slave becomes free only if the master repents.
D) The emancipation is valid but the master must pay a penalty.

Key Takeaway
Clear words of emancipation make the slave free; corrupt intentions do not block the legal effect.

Coerced and Intoxicated Emancipation: Ruling and Proof
Ruling that coercion and intoxication do not prevent emancipation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on coerced and intoxicated emancipation and explain the proof from hadith and analogy with divorce.

Core Idea
Emancipation is valid even under coercion or intoxication, just like divorce, because the act is serious and words take effect regardless of intent.

This lesson examines a specific ruling: if a master frees his slave while coerced or intoxicated, does the emancipation take effect? The Hanafi school answers yes, drawing on a hadith about three serious matters and an analogy with divorce. We will break down the ruling and its evidence, and see why coercion and intoxication do not invalidate the act.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage rules that emancipation (عتاق) by a coerced or intoxicated person is valid. The slave becomes free. Focus on the unconditional language: the act takes effect.
The term 'coerced' (مكره) means under threat of death or beating; 'intoxicated' (سكران) means drunk but aware of words.
2
Note the analogy with divorce
The author explicitly compares emancipation to divorce: just as a coerced or intoxicated divorce is valid, so is emancipation. This is a qiyas (analogical reasoning) based on shared 'illah (effective cause) – both are serious verbal acts that take effect regardless of the speaker's state.
Divorce is explicitly mentioned in the hadith; emancipation is added by analogy and also appears in a variant narration.
3
Examine the hadith proof
The hadith states: 'Three things are serious whether in jest or earnest: marriage, divorce, and return (to marriage).' Another version includes emancipation. The key point is that jest does not negate the effect; therefore, coercion and intoxication, being more severe than jest, also do not negate the effect.
The hadith is from Abu Hurairah and Abu Darda', reported in Sunan Abi Dawud, Tirmidhi, and Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah.
4
Understand the reasoning from jest to coercion/intoxication
The hadith explicitly covers jest. The author uses a fortiori reasoning: if jest (which implies no serious intention) does not invalidate, then coercion or intoxication (which impair judgment but not the utterance) certainly do not invalidate. This is known as 'فحوى الخطاب' or more specifically 'قياس أولى' (a fortiori analogy).
This reasoning is consistent with Hanafi usul: the effective cause ('illah) is the utterance of explicit words, not the mental state.
5
Consider practical implications and limits
The ruling applies to any clear declaration of emancipation under coercion or intoxication. However, if a person loses complete reason (insanity or unconsciousness), the act is not valid. The distinction is important for fatwa.
The passage does not discuss insanity; that is a separate ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[2211] (22) وعتق المكره و
زبردستی کئے گئے اور نشہ میں مست کا آزاد کرنا واقع ہو جاتا ہے۔
ایک آدمی پر زبردستی کی کہ تم اپنے غلام کو آزاد کرو ۔ اس نے قتل یا مار سے مجبور ہو کر غلام آزاد کردیا تو غلام آزاد ہو جائے گا۔ اسی طرح

[2211] (22) And the emancipation of the coerced and the intoxicated takes effect. A person was coerced: 'Free your slave!' He freed under threat of death or beating, the slave becomes free. Similarly, a person intoxicated freed his slave, the slave becomes free. The ruling of emancipation is like that of divorce. Just as divorce under coercion or intoxication takes effect, so does emancipation. Hadith: Abu Hurairah reported that the Prophet (SAW) said: 'Three things are serious whether done in earnest or in jest: marriage, divorce, and return (to marriage).' (Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi). In Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah: Abu Darda' said: 'Three things are not to be played with: marriage, emancipation, and divorce.' This hadith shows that even in jest, divorce takes effect; similarly, emancipation takes effect. The coerced and intoxicated are like the jester, so emancipation takes effect.
Source pages p. 250

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling that emancipation is valid even when the master is coerced or intoxicated. The author draws an analogy with divorce: just as a coerced or intoxicated person's divorce is effective, so is their emancipation. The proof is from the hadith that three matters are serious whether in jest or earnest: marriage, divorce, and return (or according to another narration, emancipation is included). Since jest does not negate the effect, coercion and intoxication, which are even more severe excuses, do not negate it either. The Hanafi school applies the same principle to emancipation as to divorce, based on the hadith and qiyas. This emphasizes the gravity of these verbal acts; once uttered, they take effect regardless of the mental state, except in cases of insanity or complete loss of reason (which is not covered here).

Key Terms
المكره (al-mukrah): One who is coerced under threat of harm (like death or beating) to perform an act.
السكران (al-sakrān): One who is intoxicated such that he loses control but still understands speech.
العتاق (al-'itāq): Emancipation of a slave; the act of freeing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) By analogy to divorce, which also takes effect under coercion and intoxication.
C) Because the hadith does not mention coercion or intoxication.
D) Only if the master repeats the declaration three times.

Key Takeaway
Emancipation by a coerced or intoxicated master is valid, based on the hadith and analogy with divorce.

Emancipation of a Pregnant Slave-Girl and Her Fetus
Ruling with proof from athar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on emancipating a pregnant slave-girl, explain the fetus-as-limb analogy, and apply it to scenarios involving explicit exclusion.

Core Idea
The fetus is like a limb — freeing the mother automatically frees the fetus.

This lesson examines a specific ruling in Hanafi fiqh: if a master emancipates his pregnant slave-girl, the child in her womb is also freed, even if the master explicitly excludes it. This rule is grounded in the legal analogy that the fetus is like a limb of the mother. The ruling is supported by an athar (report) from Sufyan al-Thawri. Understanding this principle clarifies the school's stance on the unity of the mother and fetus in matters of emancipation and inheritance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
This passage concerns the act of emancipating a pregnant slave-girl. The ruling is that both the slave-girl and her fetus become free immediately upon the emancipation.
2
Understand the fetus-as-limb analogy
The text uses the analogy that the fetus is like a limb (عضو) of the mother. Therefore, freeing the mother automatically includes the fetus, just as freeing a person includes all their limbs. Even if the master says 'I free her but not the fetus,' the fetus is still freed because it cannot be separated.
This is a Hukm Wad'i (declaratory ruling) — the status changes regardless of intention.
3
Recognize the proof from the Athar
The passage cites an athar from Sufyan al-Thawri: 'If he excludes what is in her womb, she is completely freed, for her child is like a limb of her.' This direct statement establishes the ruling as a transmitted proof.
The athar is recorded in Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq (no. 16800), a primary source of early hadith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا اعتق جارية حاملا عتقت وعتق حملها [2214] (25) اگر حاملہ باندی آزاد کی گئی تو وہ آزاد ہوگی اور اس کا حمل آزاد ہوگا۔ حمل باندی کے عضو کی طرح ہے اس لئے جب باندی آزاد ہوگی تو چاہے حمل کو آزاد کرنے کا انکار کیا ہو پھر بھی وہ آزاد ہو جائے گا (۲) اثر میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ قال سفيان... واذا استثني مافي بطنها عتقت كلها انما ولدها كعضو منها . واذا اعتق ما في بطنها ولم يعتقها لم يعتق الا ما في بطنها (ب) (مصنف عبد الرزاق ، باب الرجل يحق امته و یستنی مافی بطنها والرجل بیشتری ابنه ج تاسع ص ۷۲ انمبر ۱۶۸۰۰) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ حمل باندی کے عضو کی طرح ہے اس لئے حمل کا استثناء بھی کرے تب بھی وہ آزاد ہو جائے گا۔
And if he emancipates a pregnant slave-girl, she is emancipated and her fetus is emancipated. [2214] (25) If a pregnant slave-girl is emancipated, she will be free and her fetus will be free. The fetus is like a limb of the slave-girl. Therefore, when the slave-girl is freed, even if he refuses to free the fetus, it still becomes free. (2) There is proof of this in the athar. Sufyan said: ... And if he excludes what is in her womb, she is completely freed, for her child is like a limb of her. And if he frees what is in her womb and does not free her, then only what is in her womb is freed. (Mussanaf Abd al-Razzaq, Bab al-rajul yu'tiqu amatahu wa yastathni ma fi batniha, vol. 9, p. 72, no. 16800). From this athar it is known that the fetus is like a limb of the slave-girl, so even if he excludes the fetus, it still becomes free.
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This passage states the Hanafi ruling on emancipating a pregnant slave-girl. The key principle is that the fetus is considered part of the mother's body, like a limb. Therefore, when the mother is freed, the fetus is automatically freed with her, even if the master explicitly excludes the fetus from emancipation. The ruling is supported by an athar from Sufyan al-Thawri recorded in Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq. The consequence: emancipation of the mother necessarily includes the fetus, but not vice versa (as will be seen in the next ruling).

Key Terms
حمل (haml): Fetus or unborn child in the womb.
عضو (udw): Limb or body part.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Only the mother is free, the fetus remains a slave.
B) Both are free.
C) Only the fetus is free.
D) Neither is free.

Key Takeaway
Emancipating a pregnant slave-girl frees both mother and fetus because the fetus is legally analogous to a limb.

Emancipation of Only the Fetus Without the Mother
Ruling that freeing only the fetus does not free the mother.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on emancipating only the fetus and explain why the mother is not included, citing the athar and qiyas.

Core Idea
Freeing only the fetus frees the fetus; the mother remains enslaved because she is the principal, not the subordinate.

This lesson addresses a specific scenario in slave emancipation: when a master declares freedom only for the unborn child. The Hanafi position is clear—the fetus is freed, the mother is not. We will explore the ruling, its reasoning based on the principle of asl (principal) and far' (subordinate), and the proof from the athar of Ibrahim al-Nakha'i.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is emancipation of only the fetus. The ruling is that the fetus is freed, but the mother remains a slave.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the athar from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i recorded in Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, which permits excluding the fetus when freeing the mother.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
By qiyas (analogy), if excluding the fetus is valid when freeing the mother, then freeing the fetus alone is also valid. The athar indicates the separability of the two.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
This ruling is mukhtalaf fih (disputed) among madhhabs. The Hanafi school maintains the distinction based on asl-far' logic.
Other schools may hold that the mother is freed automatically.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi school relies on the transmitted athar and the principle that the mother is the principal (asl). Hence, freeing the subordinate does not imply freeing the principal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان اعتق الحمل خاصة عتق ولم تعتق الام [2215] (26) آقا نے صرف حمل آزاد کیا اور باندی کو آزاد نہیں کیا تو صرف حمل آزاد ہوگا اور باندی آزاد نہیں ہوگی۔ باندی اصل ہے اس لئے وہ حمل کے تابع نہیں ہوگی۔ اس لئے حمل کے تابع ہو کر باندی آزاد نہیں ہوگی (۲) اثر میں اس کا اشارہ ہے۔ عن ابراهيم قال اذا اعتق الرجل امته واستثنى ما في بطنها فله ما استثنى (ج) (مصنف عبدالرزاق ، باب الرجل يعتق امته ویستنی ما في بطنهاج تاسع ص ۷۲ انمبر ۱۶۸۰۰) اس اثر میں اگر چہ یہ ہے کہ باندی کو آزاد کرے اور حمل کا استثنی کرے تو جائز ہے۔ لیکن اس پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے یہ کہا جائے کہ حمل کو آزاد کرے اور باندی کا انکار کرے تو جائز ہو جائے گا۔ اوپر کے اثر میں تھا لم يعتق الا ما في بطنها ( مصنف عبدالرزاق نمبر ۱۶۸۰۰) اس سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ صرف حمل آزاد ہوگا۔
And if he emancipates the fetus specifically, it is emancipated and the mother is not emancipated. [2215] (26) The master freed only the fetus and did not free the slave-girl, so only the fetus will be free and the slave-girl will not be free. The slave-girl is the principal (asl), so she will not be subordinate to the fetus. Therefore, the slave-girl will not be freed by being subordinate to the fetus. (2) There is an indication of this in the athar. From Ibrahim: If a man emancipates his slave-girl and excludes what is in her womb, then he has what he excluded. (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, no. 16800) In this athar, although it is that if he frees the slave-girl and excludes the fetus, it is permissible. But by analogy, it can be said that if he frees the fetus and excludes the slave-girl, it is permissible. The previous athar had 'only what is in her womb is freed' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq no. 16800), from which it is also known that only the fetus is freed.
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This passage complements the previous one. It states the reverse scenario: if the master emancipates only the fetus (e.g., he says 'my slave-girl's child is free'), then only the fetus becomes free, and the mother remains a slave. The reasoning is that the mother is the principal (asl), so she does not become subordinate to the fetus. The text cites an athar from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i which, through qiyas, supports this ruling. The commentary explains that by analogy from the previous athar, freeing the fetus alone is valid and the mother is not included. Thus, the Hanafi position is consistent: the inclusion works one way only—mother includes fetus, but not vice versa.

Key Terms
اصل (asl): Principal; the original entity. Here, the mother is the principal and the fetus is subordinate.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a master says 'The fetus in my slave-girl's womb is free' but does not mention the mother, what happens?
A) Both mother and fetus are free.
B) Only the fetus is free.
C) Only the mother is free.
D) Neither is free.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, freeing only the fetus does not free the mother because the mother is the principal (asl) and the fetus is subordinate.
