Child of Slave Woman from Her Master is Free
States ruling on child of slave woman from her master, with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that a child born to a slave woman from her master is free, identify the hadith proof, and explain the consequences for the mother as umm walad.

Core Idea
A child born to a slave woman from her master is free; the mother becomes umm walad, freed upon the master's death.

This lesson examines a specific ruling from classical Hanafi fiqh concerning the legal status of a child born to a master from his own slave woman. We will explore the ruling, its proof from hadith, and the implications for the mother's status as umm walad.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the birth of a child to a slave woman from her master. The ruling states that the child is free. Note also the adjacent rulings: child from her husband is slave, child of free woman from a slave is free.
These three rulings form a coherent set based on lineage and ownership.
2
Locate the dalil
The commentator cites the hadith: 'Whoever owns a mahram relative, he becomes free.' This is an ahad hadith, so its thubut is zanni.
The hadith is recorded in Abu Dawud and Tirmidhi.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith's phrase 'فهو حر' is an imperative indicating that ownership of a mahram relative (like a son) necessitates freedom. Here, the master owns the child as his son, so the child becomes free.
The Hanafi usul principle: al-amr yufidu al-wujub.
4
Note the consequence for the mother
Because the child is free, the mother becomes umm walad. She cannot be sold and is freed upon the master's death. This is a secondary effect of the child's freedom.
Umm walad status is a key Hanafi concept.
5
Consider the epistemological weight
This is a Zahir al-Riwayah ruling with no intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf mentioned. It is the mufta bihi position and considered muttafaq alayh across schools.
The dalil is zanni in thubut but the ruling is widely accepted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[٢٢١٩] (۳۰) وولد الامة من مولاها حر ۲۲۰ (۳۱) وولدها من زوجها مملوک لسيدها (۳۲) وولد الحرة من العبد حر.

[۲۲۱۹] (۳۰) باندی کا بچہ اپنے آقا سے آزاد ہوگا۔
آقا نے اپنی باندی سے صحبت کی اور اس سے بچہ پیدا ہوا تو وہ بچہ آقا کا بیٹا ہو گا اس لئے وہ بچہ آزاد ہوگا۔ بلکہ اس کی آزادگی کی وجہ سے ماں بھی ام ولد بن جائے گی اور ماں آقا کے مرنے کے بعد آزاد ہو جائے گی۔ والد بچے کا مالک بن جائے گا کیونکہ باندی کا آقا وہی ہے اور بچے کا مالک بنا تو حدیث من ملک ذا رحم محرم فهو حر (ابوداؤد شریف، باب فیمن ملک زار تم محرم ج ۲ ص ۱۹۴ نمبر ۳۹۴۹ ، ترمذی شریف، باب ماجاء فیمن ملک زار تم محرم ص ۲۵۳ نمبر ۱۳۶۵) اس حدیث کی بنا پر بیٹا باپ پر آزاد ہو جائے گا۔
The child of a slave woman from her master is free. And the child of her (the slave woman) from her husband is the property of her master. And the child of a free woman from a slave is free.

(30) The child of a slave woman from her master will be free. The master had intercourse with his slave woman and a child was born from her, then that child will be the master's son, therefore that child will be free. Rather, because of his freedom, the mother also becomes umm walad, and the mother will become free after the master's death. The father becomes the owner of the child, because the master of the slave woman is he, and he became the owner of the child, so based on the hadith 'Whoever owns a mahram relative, he becomes free', the son becomes free from the father.
Source pages p. 254

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the matn of Al-Hidayah or similar text, followed by its commentary. The ruling states that a child born to a slave woman from her master is free. The commentator expands on this, explaining that such a child is considered the master's son and therefore free. Additionally, the mother becomes an umm walad (a slave mother of a free child), which means she will be freed upon her master's death. The proof is the hadith that if a person owns a mahram relative (like a son), that relative becomes free. This is a Zahir al-Riwayah ruling based on the hadith, and there is no mention of ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school here, so it is the mufta bihi position.

Key Terms
أمة (amah): A female slave owned by a master.
ولد (walad): Child, offspring; in this context, specifically a child born to a slave woman.
أم ولد (umm walad): A slave woman who has borne a child to her master; she is freed upon her master's death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) She remains a slave permanently.
B) She becomes free immediately.
C) She becomes umm walad and is freed upon the master's death.
D) She is sold away from the child.

Key Takeaway
A child born to a master from his slave woman is free, and the mother becomes umm walad, gaining freedom upon the master's death.

Child of Slave Woman from Her Husband is Slave of Master
States ruling on child of slave woman from her husband

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the status of a child born to a slave woman from her husband and cite the proof from the Companions' athar.

Core Idea
A child born to a slave woman follows her status — slavery, even if the father is free.

This lesson examines a clear rule from the Hanafi school: the child of a slave woman, regardless of whether her husband is free or enslaved, is born a slave belonging to her master. The rule is rooted in the principle that the child's status follows the mother, and it is supported by narrations from the Companions Ibn Umar and Ali. We will walk through the ruling, its rationale, and the evidentiary basis.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? The birth of a child from a slave woman and her husband. What is the legal status of that child? The child is the property (mamluk) of the mother's master — a slave.
The ruling applies whether the husband is free or a slave.
2
Locate the proof (dalil)
The text cites athar (Companion statements) from Ibn Umar and Ali. Ibn Umar said: 'The child of a mudabbara is freed with her freedom and enslaved with her enslavement.' Ali said concerning a mukataba: 'Her child is in her position.'
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah (how the proof proves the ruling)
These athar explicitly tie the child's status to the mother's status. Since the mother is a slave (mudabbara, mukataba, or ordinary slave), her child is a slave. The principle is that the child follows the mother in freedom and slavery.
This is a qawl sahabi, which is a source of law in the Hanafi school when not contradicted.
4
Note the nature of the proof
The athar are transmitted with zanni thubut (not mutawatir) and their dalala (indication) is also zanni (open to interpretation). However, they are accepted as valid evidence in the Hanafi school.
5
Recognize the practical application
In practice, if a master marries his slave woman to a man, any child born belongs to the master as a slave. The child's lineage is established to the father, but its ownership and status are with the mother's master.
This ruling is zahir al-riwayah and mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۲۲۰] (۳۱) اور باندی کا بچہ اپنے شوہر سے اس کے آقا کا مملوک ہوگا۔
آقا نے اپنی باندی کی شادی کسی آدمی سے کرائی چاہے وہ آدمی آزاد ہو یا غلام۔ اس آدمی سے باندی کو بچہ ہوا تو اس بچے کا نسب باپ سے ثابت ہوگا لیکن بچہ باندی کے تابع ہو کر آقا کا غلام ہوگا۔
اثر میں ہے کہ مدبرہ اور مکاتبہ کا بچہ ماں کے تابع ہو کر غلام اور باندی بنے گا۔ اثر میں ہے۔ عن ابن عمر قال ولد المدبرة يعتقون بعتقها ويرقون برقها (دارقطنی، کتاب المکاتب، ج رابع ص ۷۷ نمبر ۴۲۱۳ سن للبیہقی ، باب ماجاء فی ولد المد برة من غير سیدھا بعد تدبیر هاج عاشر ص ۵۳۱ نمبر ۲۱۵۸۴) (۲) اثر میں ہے۔ عن على قال ولدها بمنزلتها يعنى المكاتبة ستن ليبقى ، باب ولد المكاتب من جاریبتہ وولد المكاسبة من زوجهاج عاشر ص ۵۶۰ نمبر ۲۱۶۹۹) اس اثر سے بھی معلوم ہوا مکاتبہ کا بچہ مکاتبہ کے درجے میں ہے اسی طرح باندی کا بچہ غلام ہوگا۔
(31) And the child of the slave woman from her husband will be the property of her master.
The master married his slave woman to some man, whether that man is free or a slave. A child was born to the slave woman from that man, then that child's lineage is established from the father, but the child, following the mother, becomes a slave of the master.
There is an athar that the child of a mudabbara and mukataba becomes a slave or slave woman following the mother. There is an athar from Ibn Umar who said: 'The child of a mudabbara is freed with her freedom and enslaved with her enslavement.' (Darqutni, al-Bayhaqi) (2) There is an athar from Ali who said: 'Her child is in her position, meaning the mukataba.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi) This athar also indicates that the child of a mukataba is in the same position as the mukataba; similarly, the child of a slave woman will be a slave.
Source pages p. 254

Commentary
This passage presents the second ruling from the matn, with commentary explaining that a child born to a slave woman from any husband (whether the husband is free or a slave) belongs to the master as a slave. The child's lineage is traced to the father, but its status (slavery) follows the mother, as she is a slave. The commentator supports this with athar (narrations from Companions) regarding mudabbara (a slave promised freedom upon master's death) and mukataba (a slave in a contract of manumission). In both cases, the child's status follows that of the mother. This is a Zahir al-Riwayah ruling, and the mufta bihi position is as stated.

Key Terms
مدبرة (mudabbara): A slave woman who has been promised freedom upon her master's death (tadbir).
مكاتبة (mukataba): A slave woman who has entered a contract of manumission (kitabah), working to earn her freedom.
مملوك (mamluk): Property, slave; in this context, the child is owned by the mother's master.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, who does the child of a slave woman from her husband belong to?
A) The father, if he is free.
B) The mother, as her child.
C) The mother's master.
D) The state.

Key Takeaway
The child of a slave woman follows the mother's status; if she is a slave, the child is a slave of her master.

Child of Free Woman from a Slave is Free
States ruling on child of free woman from a slave

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on the child of a free woman from a slave and explain the principle that the child's status follows the mother's status.

Core Idea
A child's freedom follows the mother: the child of a free woman is free even if the father is a slave.

This lesson addresses a key principle in Hanafi family law: the status of a child born to a free woman and a slave husband. While lineage may be traced to the father, freedom is determined by the mother's status. The text establishes this ruling based on the principle that the child follows the mother, supported by an athar from Sayyidina Ali (RA).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
What is the specific scenario? A free woman marries a slave and gives birth. What is the hukm for the child?
The act is the birth of a child from a free mother and slave father.
2
Locate the dalil
The text cites an athar (statement) that the child follows the mother's status. What is the evidence?
The principle 'the child is dependent on the mother and takes her status' is the dalil.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the principle apply here? Since the mother is free, the child is free.
The reasoning is that the child's condition mirrors the mother's condition.
4
Note the intra-madhhab consistency
The footnote extends the same principle to a mukataba (slave with a freedom contract). Understand the application.
The child of a mukataba follows her status, remaining a mukataba.
5
Evaluate the cross-madhhab status
Is this ruling agreed upon by all schools? The source says it is muttafaq alayh (agreed upon).
Most schools agree on this principle, though there may be minor variations.

This is supported by the principle derived from the athar that the child follows the mother's status. The footnote reiterates the same principle for a mukataba. This is a Zahir al-Riwayah ruling.

مکاتبہ (mukataba): A slave who has a contract to earn freedom by paying installments.

Ruling on the Child of a Mukataba
Statement from Ali on the status of a mukataba's child

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling regarding the status of a child born to a female mukataba and identify its source in the statement of Ali.

Core Idea
The child of a mukataba follows her status — also a mukataba.

This brief ruling from Ali (RA) clarifies the legal status of children born to a mukataba. It is a foundational rule in Hanafi kitaba law: the child is not free, but acquires the same contractual status as the mother. The ruling is transmitted from a Companion and adopted by the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal actor
The passage concerns a 'mukataba' — a female slave under a kitaba contract. Understand her hybrid status: part slave, part free.
2
Extract the ruling
The passage states: 'Her child is in her status.' This means the child shares the mother's legal classification.
3
State the implication
The child becomes a mukataba (male) or mukataba (female) like the mother. The child is bound by the same contract terms.
This does not mean the child is free; the contract must still be fulfilled.
4
Identify the source authority
The ruling is attributed to Ali ibn Abi Talib (RA). In Hanafi fiqh, statements of Companions (qawl al-sahabi) are considered a proof (hujja) when not contradicted.
The footnote confirms the attribution.

Tadbir: The Ruling and Proof that a Mudabbar Cannot Be Sold
Complete chapter on tadbir with hadith proofs and Shafi'i dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on selling a mudabbar, cite the key hadith proof, and explain why the Shafi'i position is not adopted.

Core Idea
A mudabbar cannot be sold — the right to freedom vests upon the master's declaration.

This lesson examines the chapter on tadbir (manumission upon death). We will learn what makes a slave mudabbar, the immediate legal effect that prohibits sale and gift, and the explicit hadith evidence that overrides the Shafi'i counter-argument. Understanding this ruling highlights how a vested future right restricts present ownership.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is selling (or gifting) a mudabbar slave. According to the text, the ruling is 'la yajuz' — it is not permissible. In Hanafi terminology, the sale is batil (invalid).
Batil means the contract has no legal effect; ownership does not transfer.
2
Locate the dalil
The text cites the hadith of Ibn 'Umar: 'The mudabbar is not to be sold nor gifted, and he is free from one-third.' This is the primary proof for the Hanafi position.
The hadith is ahad but its meaning is clear (dalala qati).
3
Analyse the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit negation 'la yuba' wa la yuhab' directly prohibits sale and gift. The phrase 'wa huwa hurr min al-thuluth' confirms his freed status, reinforcing that the right to freedom prevents transfer.
In Hanafi usul, the imperative or explicit prohibition gives a definitive ruling.
4
Examine the ikhtilaf with Shafi'i
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that a mudabbar can be sold, based on the hadith of Jabir where the Prophet sold a mudabbar. The Hanafi response distinguishes: the hadith of Ibn 'Umar is explicit; the Jabir hadith is ambiguous and the slave died that year, possibly nullifying the sale's effect.
The practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf): under Shafi'i, the master can sell, ending the tadbir; under Hanafi, he cannot.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The mufta bihi (operative ruling) is that a mudabbar cannot be sold or gifted. This is the position of the Zahir al-Riwayah and is supported by the explicit hadith.
No tarjih authority is named in this text, but the ruling is established.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب التدبير ) [۲۲۲۲] (۱) اذا قال المولى لمملوكه اذا مت فانت حر او انت حر عن دبر منى او انت مدبر او قد دبَّرتک فقد صار مدبرا [۲۲۲۳ (۲) لا يجوز بيعه ولا هبته. باب التدبير ضروری نون مدبر کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ آقا کہے کہ میرے مرنے کے بعد فلاں غلام یا باندی آزاد ہے تو اس کو مد بر کہتے ہیں۔ دبر کے معنی ہیں بعد میں ۔ چونکہ مرنے کے بعد آزاد کیا اس لئے اس کو مد بر کہتے ہیں۔ اس کا ثبوت اس حدیث میں ہے۔ عن جابر بن عبد الله قال اعتق رجل منا عبدا له عن دبر فدعا النبي الا الله فباعه قال جابر مات الغلام عام اول (الف) ( بخاری شریف، باب بیع المد برص ۳۴۴ نمبر ۲۵۳۴، ابوداؤد شریف ، باب فی بیع المد بر ص ۱۹۵ نمبر ۳۹۵۵) (۲) دوسری حدیث میں ہے۔ عن ابن عمر ان النبی قال المدبر لا يباع ولا يوهب وهو حر من الثلث (ب) (دار قطنی ، کتاب المكاتب ج رابع ص ۷۸ نمبر ۴۲۲۰ ) اس دونوں حدیثوں سے مد بر بنانے کا ثبوت ہے۔ [۲۲۲۲) (۱) اگر آقا نے اپنے مملوک سے کہا جب میں مروں تو تم آزاد ہو یا تم میرے مرنے کے بعد آزاد ہو یا تم مدبر ہو یا میں نے تم کو مدبر بنا دیا تو وہ مدبر ہو جائے گا۔ یہ سب الفاظ صریح طور پر مد بر بنانے کے ہیں۔ مثلا یوں کہے کہ جب میں مرجاؤں تو تم آزاد ہو تو ان الفاظ سے صراحت کے طور پر د بر بنایا ہوا۔ ان سے غلام مدبر ہو جائے گا۔ ۲۲۲۳۱) (۲) نہیں جائز ہے مدبر کو بیچنا اور نہ اس کو ہبہ کرنا۔ جب غلام کود بر بنا دیا تواب اس کو بچنا اوراس کو ہبہ کرنا یا انی ملکیت سے نکالنا جائز نہیں ہے صرف آزاد کر سکتا ہے۔ او پر حدیث میں ہے۔ عن ابن عمر ان النبی الا الله قال المدبر لا يباع ولا يوهب وهو حر من الثلث (دار قطني ، كتاب المكاتب ج رابع ص ۷۸ نمبر ۴۲۲۰ سن لیبقی ، باب من قال لا یباع المد برج عاشر ص ۵۲۹ نمبر ۲۱۵۷۲) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ وہ آزاد ہے اس کو نہ بیچا جاسکتا ہے اور نہ ہبہ کر سکتا ہے (۲) اس میں آزادگی کا شائبہ آ چکا ہے اس لئے بیچ کر اس کو ختم نہیں کر سکتا۔ امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ مدبر کو بیچ سکتا ہے۔ ان کی دلیل اوپر کی حدیث ہے۔ عن جابر بن عبد الله قال اعتق رجل منا عبدا له عن دبر فدعا النبي الله فباعه (ج) حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت جابر فرماتے ہیں کہ ہم میں سے ایک آدمی نے اپنے غلام کو مد بر بنایا تو حضور نے ان کو بلایا اور غلام کو بیچ دیا۔ حضرت جابر فرماتے ہیں کہ غلام پہلے سال میں انتقال کر گیا (ب) آپ نے فرمایا مد بر نہ بیچا جاسکتا ہے اور نہ ہبہ کیا جاسکتا ہے دو تہائی مال میں سے آزاد ہے (ج) حضرت جابر فرماتے ہیں کہ ہم میں سے ایک آدمی نے اپنے غلام کود بر بنایا تو حضور نے اس کو بلایا اور اس کو بیچا۔
Chapter of Tadbir. [2222] (1) When the master says to his slave: 'When I die, you are free' or 'You are free from my back' or 'You are mudabbar' or 'I have made you mudabbar', then he becomes mudabbar. [2223] (2) It is not permissible to sell him nor to gift him. (Urdu explanation) The meaning of tadbir is that the master says: 'After my death, such-and-such slave or slave-girl is free.' The word dubr means after. Since he is freed after death, he is called mudabbar. Its proof is in this hadith: From Jabir ibn 'Abdullah: 'A man among us freed his slave as a mudabbar, so the Prophet called him and sold him.' Jabir said: 'The slave died in the first year.' (Bukhari, Abu Dawud) (2) Another hadith: From Ibn 'Umar that the Prophet said: 'The mudabbar is not to be sold nor gifted, and he is free from one-third.' (Dar Qutni) From these two hadiths, the basis of tadbir is established. [2222] (1) If the master says to his slave: 'When I die, you are free' or 'You are free after my death' or 'You are mudabbar' or 'I have made you mudabbar', then he becomes mudabbar. These are all explicit words for making tadbir. [2223] (2) It is not permissible to sell a mudabbar nor to gift him. When the slave is made mudabbar, then selling him, gifting him, or removing him from ownership is not permissible; only freeing him is allowed. The above hadith indicates that. Imam al-Shafi'i says that a mudabbar can be sold. His proof is the above hadith of Jabir. Footnotes: (a) Jabir said: A man made his slave mudabbar, so the Prophet called him and sold the slave. Jabir said: The slave died in the first year. (b) He said: The mudabbar is not to be sold nor gifted, and he is free from one-third. (c) Jabir said: A man made his slave mudabbar, so the Prophet called him and sold him.
Source pages p. 256

Commentary
This is the chapter on tadbir (manumission upon death) from a Hanafi fiqh text. The passage begins by defining tadbir as the master's declaration that his slave will be free after his death. The word 'dubr' means after, hence the slave is called mudabbar. The legal basis (thubut) is established by two hadith: (1) the hadith of Jabir ibn 'Abdullah where the Prophet sold a mudabbar slave (this is used by Imam al-Shafi'i as evidence that sale is permissible), and (2) the hadith of Ibn 'Umar where the Prophet explicitly said that a mudabbar cannot be sold or gifted, and he is free from one-third of the master's estate. The author then explains the explicit wording that creates tadbir: any clear statement indicating freedom after death makes the slave mudabbar. Once a slave is made mudabbar, he cannot be sold, gifted, or transferred out of ownership; only manumission is possible. The author then presents a disagreement: Imam al-Shafi'i argues that a mudabbar can be sold, citing the hadith of Jabir where the Prophet sold one. The Hanafi response is implicit: they rely on the hadith of Ibn 'Umar which explicitly prohibits sale, and they note that in Jabir's hadith, the slave died that year, possibly indicating that the sale was not effective or was a specific case. Thus, the Hanafi position is that a mudabbar cannot be sold, and this is the relied-upon view (mufta bihi).

Key Terms
مدبر (mudabbar): A slave who has been promised freedom upon the death of his master by the master's declaration.
تدبير (tadbīr): The act of making a slave mudabbar, i.e., declaring that he will be free after the master's death.
لا يجوز (lā yajūz): It is not permissible; the act is invalid or prohibited.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, what is the ruling on selling a mudabbar slave?
A) It is permissible.
B) It is not permissible.
C) It is permissible only with the slave's consent.
D) It is permissible if the master needs money.

Key Takeaway
A mudabbar slave cannot be sold or gifted because his right to freedom has already vested upon the master's declaration, supported by the explicit hadith of Ibn 'Umar.

The Mudabbar Dispute: Sale and Gift Prohibition
States Hanafi ruling and Shafi'i opposing view with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on selling a mudabbar and explain the Shafi'i counter-argument using their respective proofs.

Core Idea
A mudabbar cannot be sold or gifted because he already bears a right to freedom, and the explicit hadith of Ibn Umar forbids it.

The mudabbar is a slave whose freedom is deferred to the master's death. This creates a unique legal status: the slave is not yet free, but a vested right to freedom has attached. The Hanafi school holds that this right cannot be undone by sale or gift, while the Shafi'i school disagrees. This lesson unpacks the evidence each side uses and the practical consequence of their difference.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the exact ruling: the mudabbar cannot be sold or gifted. Determine why—because a 'taint of freedom' (shaa'ibat al-hurriyya) has entered him, making such transactions invalid.
The ruling is explicit in the text: 'لا يجوز بيعه ولا هبته'.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the mudabbar can be sold. Note his evidence: the hadith of Jabir where the Prophet sold a mudabbar.
Opponent: Imam al-Shafi'i.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine the hadith of Jabir: a man made his slave mudabbar, then the Prophet called him and sold the slave. This appears to directly contradict the Hanafi position.
Source: 'فدعا النبي فباعه' – the Prophet sold him.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school prefers the hadith of Ibn Umar ('لا يباع ولا يوهب') because it is more explicit. The Jabir incident may have been abrogated, or was a special case (e.g., the master was in need). The right to freedom cannot be removed by sale.
Hanafi scholars prioritize clarity and the principle that a right to freedom is irrevocable.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: under Hanafi, the mudabbar remains in ownership with an inalienable right to freedom; under Shafi'i, the owner can sell, terminating the tadbir.
This affects estate planning and the slave's status.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۲۲۳] (۲) لا يجوز بيعه ولا هبته. جب غلام کود بر بنا دیا تواب اس کو بچنا اوراس کو ہبہ کرنا یا انی ملکیت سے نکالنا جائز نہیں ہے صرف آزاد کر سکتا ہے۔ او پر حدیث میں ہے۔ عن ابن عمر ان النبی الا الله قال المدبر لا يباع ولا يوهب وهو حر من الثلث (دار قطني ، كتاب المكاتب ج رابع ص ۷۸ نمبر ۴۲۲۰ سن لیبقی ، باب من قال لا یباع المد برج عاشر ص ۵۲۹ نمبر ۲۱۵۷۲) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ وہ آزاد ہے اس کو نہ بیچا جاسکتا ہے اور نہ ہبہ کر سکتا ہے (۲) اس میں آزادگی کا شائبہ آ چکا ہے اس لئے بیچ کر اس کو ختم نہیں کر سکتا۔ امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ مدبر کو بیچ سکتا ہے۔ ان کی دلیل اوپر کی حدیث ہے۔ عن جابر بن عبد الله قال اعتق رجل منا عبدا له عن دبر فدعا النبي الله فباعه (ج) حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت جابر فرماتے ہیں کہ ہم میں سے ایک آدمی نے اپنے غلام کو مد بر بنایا تو حضور نے ان کو بلایا اور غلام کو بیچ دیا۔ حضرت جابر فرماتے ہیں کہ غلام پہلے سال میں انتقال کر گیا (ب) آپ نے فرمایا مد بر نہ بیچا جاسکتا ہے اور نہ ہبہ کیا جاسکتا ہے دو تہائی مال میں سے آزاد ہے (ج) حضرت جابر فرماتے ہیں کہ ہم میں سے ایک آدمی نے اپنے غلام کو مد بر بنایا تو حضور نے اس کو بلایا اور اس کو بیچا۔
[2223] (2) It is not permissible to sell him or gift him. When a slave is made mudabbar, then selling him, gifting him, or removing him from ownership is not permissible. He can only be freed. The hadith about it: from Ibn Umar that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'The mudabbar cannot be sold nor given as a gift, and he is free from one-third.' (Darqutni, Kitab al-Mukatib, vol. 4 p. 78 no. 4220; Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Bab Man Qala La Yuba' al-Mudabbar, vol. 10 p. 529 no. 21572) From this hadith, it is known that he (the mudabbar) is free, he cannot be sold or gifted. A hint of freedom has come into him, so selling him cannot eliminate it. Imam Shafi'i says that the mudabbar can be sold. His proof is the above hadith: from Jabir ibn Abdullah: 'A man among us manumitted a male slave of his as mudabbar, and the Prophet (peace be upon him) called him and sold him.' (c) Footnote: (a) Jabir said: A man among us made his slave mudabbar, and the Prophet called him and sold the slave. Jabir said: The slave died in the first year. (b) He said: The mudabbar cannot be sold or gifted, he is free from two-thirds of the wealth. (c) Jabir said: A man among us made his slave mudabbar, and the Prophet called him and sold him.
Source pages p. 256

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute. The Hanafi position is that once a slave is made mudabbar, he cannot be sold or gifted because he has a vested right to freedom upon the master's death. The proof is the hadith of Ibn Umar which explicitly forbids these transactions. The underlying reasoning is that the mudabbar already has a 'taint' of freedom (shaa'ibat al-hurriyya) that cannot be undone by sale. Imam Shafi'i disagrees, arguing from the hadith of Jabir where the Prophet himself sold a mudabbar. The text includes a footnote citing both hadith. The Hanafi school resolves this by preferring the Ibn Umar hadith for its explicit prohibition, or by interpreting the Jabir incident as a special case before the prohibition was known, or as an exception for necessity. The text does not give the Hanafi response explicitly, but the author clearly adheres to the Hanafi view.

Key Terms
مدبر (mudabbar): A slave whose freedom is tied to the master's death, cannot be sold or gifted.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why can a mudabbar not be sold?
A) Because he is already free
B) Because he has a taint of freedom
C) Because selling is not allowed for any slave
D) Because the master has no right to sell

Key Takeaway
The mudabbar cannot be sold or gifted because the explicit hadith of Ibn Umar prohibits it, and a vested right to freedom cannot be undone.

Permissibility for Master to Use Mudabbar's Services and Intercourse
Ruling that the master retains the right to use, hire, and have intercourse with the mudabbar slave.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rights a master retains over a mudabbar slave and identify the proofs from hadith and athar that justify these rights.

Core Idea
The mudabbar is still a slave; the master retains all ownership rights except sale and gift.

This passage clarifies the legal status of a mudabbar (a slave promised freedom upon the master's death). Despite the promise of future freedom, the slave is still fully owned in the present. Therefore, the master may continue to exercise rights of ownership such as using the slave's service, hiring him out, and if female, having intercourse or arranging her marriage. These rights are supported by specific textual proofs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and their ruling
The text lists four specific acts: using the mudabbar for service, hiring him out, having intercourse with a female mudabbara, and marrying her off. All are ruled permissible (mubah) because the mudabbar remains a slave.
These rights are not exhaustive; the master retains all ownership rights except those explicitly prohibited like sale.
2
Locate the proof for permissible service and hiring
The hadith from Jabir (Darqutni) states: 'There is no harm in selling the service of a mudabbar when in need.' Selling service implies that using service is also permissible, and hiring out is analogous to selling service.
The hadith is a sunnah ahad, zanni in transmission.
3
Locate the proof for permissible intercourse
The athar from Ibn Umar (Bayhaqi) narrates that he had two female mudabbar slaves and would have intercourse with them while they were mudabbar. This shows the permissibility of intercourse.
Athar refers to a tradition from a Companion, considered a proof in Hanafi fiqh.
4
Understand the implied rationale
The underlying legal principle is that the mudabbar is still a slave until the master's death. Therefore, the master's ownership rights continue, including the right to use, hire, and have intercourse.
The mudabbar is not fully free; he is only promised freedom upon a future event.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۲۲۴] (۳) وللمولى ان يستخدمه ويواجره وان كانت امة فله ان يطأها وله ان يزوجها
آقا کے لئے جائز ہے کہ مدبر سے خدمت لے اور اس کو اجرت پر رکھے۔ اور باندی ہو تو اس سے صحبت کر سکتا ہے۔ اور اس کے لئے جائز ہے کہ مدبرہ کی شادی کرائے۔ مد بر غلام آقا کے مرنے کے بعد آزاد ہو گا ابھی تو وہ غلام ہی ہے اس لئے اس کے آقا کے لئے جائز ہے کہ مدبر سے خدمت لے۔ اس کو اجرت پر رکھے۔ باندی ہو تو اس سے صحبت کرے یا باندی کی شادی دوسرے سے کرادے۔
ہے وہ غلام اور باندی ابھی بھی ہیں۔ آزاد آقا کے مرنے کے بعد ہوں گے اس لئے ابھی ان کے ساتھ غلام باندی کا معاملہ کر سکے گا۔ حدیث میں ہے۔ عـن جـابـر بن عبد الله قال رسول الله الا الله لا بأس ببيع خدمة المدبر اذا احتاج (الف)(دارقطنی ، کتاب المكاتب ج رابع ص ۷ ۷ے نمبر ۴۲۱۷) جب مدبر کی خدمت بیچ سکتا ہے تو اس سے خدمت کروا سکتا ہے۔ اس اثر سے یہ بھی معلوم ہوا کہ مدبر کو اجرت پر رکھ سکتا ہے۔ ولی کرنے کی دلیل یہ اثر ہے۔ عن ابن عمر انه دبر جاريتين له فكان يطؤهما وهما مدبرتان (ب)
(سن للمبيبقى ، باب ولی المد بر ة ج عاشر ص ۵۳۰ نمبر (۲۱۵۸) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ آقامد برہ سے ولی کر سکتا ہے۔
[2224] (3) And for the master, it is permissible to use him (the mudabbar) for service and to hire him out; if it is a female slave, then for him to have intercourse with her, and for him to marry her off. The master may take service from the mudabbar and hire him out. If she is a female slave, he may have intercourse with her or marry her off to someone else. The male and female mudabbar are still slaves; they become free only after the master's death. Therefore, he can still deal with them as slaves. In a hadith: from Jabir ibn Abdullah that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'There is no harm in selling the service of a mudabbar when in need.' (Darqutni, Kitab al-Mukatib, vol. 4 p. 77 no. 4217) Since one can sell his service, one can also take service from him. From this athar, it is also learned that he can hire him out. The proof for intercourse is this athar: from Ibn Umar that he made two of his female slaves mudabbar, and he would have intercourse with them while they were mudabbar. (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Bab Wati' al-Mudabbara, vol. 10 p. 530 no. 2158) From this athar, it is learned that the master can have intercourse with the female mudabbara.
Source pages p. 257

Commentary
This ruling establishes that the mudabbar, despite having a future right to freedom, remains a full slave in the present. The master retains all rights of ownership except those explicitly prohibited (sale and gift). The text mentions three specific rights: using the slave for personal service, hiring the slave out to others for wages, and in the case of a female slave, having sexual relations with her or arranging her marriage. The latter two are supported by athar (traditions from the Companions). The hadith from Jabir permits selling the service of a mudabbar, implying that using his service is also allowed. The practice of Ibn Umar shows that one can have intercourse with a female mudabbara. These rights exist because the mudabbar is still owned.

Key Terms
استخدام (istikhdām): Making use of the slave's labor for personal service.
وطء (waṭʾ): Sexual intercourse with a female mudabbara.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the basis for permitting the master to hire out a mudabbar?
A) Qiyas with free persons
B) The hadith allowing sale of his service
C) General permissibility of hiring
D) The mudabbar is not a slave

Key Takeaway
The master retains all ownership rights over a mudabbar slave except sale and gift, because the slave's freedom is only in the future.

Master's Rights Over a Mudabbar: Use, Hire, Intercourse
Ruling on permissible actions of master with mudabbar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three permissible actions a master may perform with a mudabbar and cite the two proofs from hadith and athar.

Core Idea
A mudabbar remains a slave during the master's lifetime, so all ownership rights continue.

In this lesson, we examine a ruling from the chapter of tadbir (declaration of freedom upon death). The text clarifies that although the slave has been promised freedom after the master's death, the master retains full ownership during his lifetime. Thus, he may utilize the mudabbar's labor, hire him out, and if the mudabbar is female, engage in intercourse and arrange her marriage. The proofs are drawn from sound transmitted reports.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What specific actions are being ruled upon? The passage states the master may: 1) take service from the mudabbar, 2) hire him out, 3) have intercourse with a female mudabbarah, and 4) marry her off. The ruling is permissible (mubah).
The ruling is based on the continued slave status of the mudabbar.
2
Locate the first dalil
The text cites a hadith from Jabir ibn Abdullah: 'There is no harm in selling the service of a mudabbar when needed.' This indicates that using his service (including hiring) is allowed.
The hadith is from Darqutni.
3
Locate the second dalil
The text cites the practice of Ibn Umar, who made two slave-girls mudabbars and continued to have intercourse with them. This proves the permissibility of intercourse with a mudabbarah.
The athar is from Sunan al-Bayhaqi.
4
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How do these proofs yield the ruling? The hadith explicitly permits selling service, which implies that the master can also use the service himself (arguably a lesser action). The athar directly shows the master's right to intercourse. Both rely on the fact that the mudabbar remains a slave.
The logic is that what is allowed for a third party (selling service) is allowed for the master.
5
Note the intellectual consistency
The passage reaffirms the Hanafi principle that tadbir does not alter the slave's status until death. The ruling is unanimous within the Hanafi school (zahir al-riwayah).
No intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf is reported here.

[۲۲۲٤] (۳) وللمولى ان يستخدمه ويواجره وان كانت امة فله ان يطأها وله ان يزوجها (بخاری شریف ، باب بیع المد بر ص ۱۳٤٤ نمبر ۲۵۳٤، ابو داؤد شریف، باب فی بیع المد بر ص ۱۹۵ نمبر ۳۹۵۵) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ مدبر کو بیچا اس لئے مدبر کو بیچنا جائز ہے۔
۲۲۲٤] (۳) اور آقا کے لئے جائز ہے کہ مدبر سے خدمت لے اور اس کو اجرت پر رکھے۔ اور باندی ہو تو اس سے صحبت کر سکتا ہے۔ اور اس کے لئے جائز ہے کہ مدبرہ کی شادی کرائے۔ مد بر غلام آقا کے مرنے کے بعد آزاد ہو گا ابھی تو وہ غلام ہی ہے اس لئے اس کے آقا کے لئے جائز ہے کہ مدبر سے خدمت لے۔ اس کو اجرت پر رکھے۔ باندی ہو تو اس سے صحبت کرے یا باندی کی شادی دوسرے سے کرادے۔
۔
ہے وہ غلام اور باندی ابھی بھی ہیں۔ آزاد آقا کے مرنے کے بعد ہوں گے اس لئے ابھی ان کے ساتھ غلام باندی کا معاملہ کر سکے گا۔ حدیث میں ہے۔ عـن جـابـر بن عبد الله قال رسول الله الا الله لا بأس ببيع خدمة المدبر اذا احتاج (الف)(دارقطنی ، کتاب المكاتب ج رابع ص ۷ ۷ے نمبر ٤۲۱۷) جب مدبر کی خدمت بیچ سکتا ہے تو اس سے خدمت کروا سکتا ہے۔ اس اثر سے یہ بھی معلوم ہوا کہ مدبر کو اجرت پر رکھ سکتا ہے۔ ولی کرنے کی دلیل یہ اثر ہے۔ عن ابن عمر انه دبر جاريتين له فكان يطؤهما وهما مدبرتان (ب)
(سن للمبيبقى ، باب ولی المد بر ة ج عاشر ص ۵۳۰ نمبر (۲۱۵۸) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ آقامد برہ سے ولی کر سکتا ہے.
The master may use his services and hire him out; if she is a female slave, he may have intercourse with her and he may marry her off. (Bukhari, chapter on selling mudabbar p.1344 no.2534; Abu Dawud, chapter on selling mudabbar p.195 no.3955) This hadith states that a mudabbar was sold, so selling a mudabbar is permissible. And for the master it is permissible to take service from the mudabbar and hire him out. If she is a female slave, he can have intercourse with her and he can arrange her marriage. The mudabbar slave will be freed after the master's death; now he is still a slave, so it is permissible for the master to take service from the mudabbar, hire him out, if female have intercourse, or marry her off to another. They are still male and female slaves; they will be freed after the master's death, so now he can treat them as slaves. The hadith states: Jabir ibn Abdullah reported that the Messenger of Allah said: There is no harm in selling the service of a mudabbar when needed. (Darqutni) Since he can sell his service, he can take service from him. This tradition also shows that he can hire him out. The evidence for intercourse is the tradition of Ibn Umar that he made two of his slave-girls mudabbars and used to have intercourse with them while they were mudabbars. (Sunan al-Bayhaqi) This tradition shows that the master can have intercourse with the mudabbarah.
Source pages p. 257

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof from the chapter of tadbir. The text establishes that despite the declaration of tadbir (which will free the slave upon the master's death), the mudabbar remains a slave during the master's lifetime. Hence, all rights of ownership continue. The master may use his labor, hire him out, and if the mudabbar is female, he may have intercourse with her and also arrange her marriage. The proof is drawn from two athar: first, a hadith from Jabir that selling the service of a mudabbar is permissible when needed, which implies using his service is allowed; second, the practice of Ibn Umar who had intercourse with his mudabbar slave-girls. Both confirm that the mudabbar's status as a slave is intact. The commentary explains that the mudabbar is essentially a slave until death, so the master's rights are unaffected.

Key Terms
مدبر (mudabbar): A slave who has been promised freedom upon the master's death, as per the declaration of tadbir.
تدبير (tadbir): The act of a master declaring that his slave will be free after his death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, is it permissible for the master to hire out his mudabbar slave?
A) No, because the mudabbar is already free.
B) Yes, because the mudabbar is still a slave.
C) Only if the mudabbar agrees.
D) Yes, but only for non-commercial work.

Key Takeaway
A mudabbar is still a slave until the master's death, so the master may use his services, hire him out, and have intercourse with a female mudabbarah.
